1. Foreword
1.1 Background
At the beginning of 1994, the Jiangxi Provincial Government made a major
decision of "Building Nanchang-Zhangshu-Jian-Ganzhou-Gan-Yue Border Special
Motorway . This road project will play very important role in the opening of the
Jiangxi province to the outside world, improvement of the investment environment,
further adjustment of the industry structure and the local people' s living standards.
As requested by the Jiangxi Provincial Communications Department (JPCD), the
Jiangxi Provincial Communications Design Institute (JPCDI) started the preparation
work of the road project in September 1994, and completed the i Feasibility Study
Report for Gan-Yue Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section)", in December 1999. In
May 2000, JPCDI compiled the supplementary report to the " Feasibility Study
Report for Gan-Yue Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section)", ,and completed the two-
stage preliminary design in July, 2000.
In December 1999 JPCD and Jiangxi Provincial Expressway Administration
(JPEA) entrusted the Research Institute of Highway (RIOH) of the MOC to undertake
the EIA work for the road project of Gan-Yue Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section),
From December 1999 to August 2000, with the assistance from the JPCDI and the
local governments and the relevant departments the EIA team from the RIOH studied
the feasibility study report and primarily design in details, conducted several times
of the site reconnaissance along the proposed highway area for the environmental
conditions and the major environmental protection targets and collection of related
materials and data.
In December 1999, the RIOH of MOC completed the TOR of EIA for this project.
In March 2000, the RIOH compiled the EIA report (first version) of Gan-Yue
Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section). On April 14, 2000, the NEPA approved by the
TOR in Document 58# [2000]. In June 2000, in accordance with the aide-memoire of
the World Bank environmental experts at the first preparation mission. the RIOH
completed the EIA report (second version) of Gan-Yue Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou
Section). On June 27, the EIA report of this project (including linking roads) passed
the examination by the environmental experts at the meeting held by the
Environmental Protection Office of MOC in Beijing. In accordance with the aide-
memoire requiremenst of the World Bank environmental experts at the second
preparation mission. we completed the EIA report (third version) of Gan-Yue
Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section). In December 2000, the EIA team completed
the EIA report (fourth version) of Gan-Yue Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section) in
accordance with the aide-memoire requirements of the World Bank environmental
experts at the pre-evaluation mission.

1.3 Environmental selection and assessment category
In accordance with the World Bank Operational Policy (OP 4.01), this project is
classified as Category A project which requires detailed and thorough environmental
assessment.
Special topic assessment category and basis are presented in Table 1-1 in
accordance with the EIA Technique Guidelines. The assessment focuses on the
ecological environment impact (including soil erosion) during the construction phase.
acoustic environrnent impact during the operation phase. alignment alternatives
comparison. environment management. monitoring plan and public consultation, etc.

1.5 Assessment time horizon
Taking into consideration the engineering design, construction and operation
period as well as the time horizon of the traffic forecast in the feasibility study report,
the year of 2004, 2015 and 2023 are to represent the initial operation period, the mid-
term operation period and the long-term operation period respectively.
1.6 Assessment method
In accordance with the World Bank Operational Policy (OP 4.01), this project will
mainly take EIA, risk appraisal and some method of EMP.
Based on the site reconnaissance, besides a few highly environmental sensitive
locations as residential quarters, schools, high- fill and deep-cut sections, the rest
sections have similarities in environmental conditions. Therefore. the assessment shall
follow the principle of "taking typical points and road sections as representatives, to
feed back for whole route .
(I) Section assessment: analysis and assessment by road sections will be
undertaken according to the characteristics of the traffic forecast. project quantities,
landforrn and meteorological environment stated in the feasibilitv study report;
(2) The acoustic and ambient air impact assessment in operation period will be
analyzed and calculated mainly by model forecast. As for the ecological environment,
water environment and soil erosion, a combination of survey . analogue analysis and
model forecast will be applied; while investigation -analysis method will be adopted
for societal environment, living standard and public participation.
(3) Assessment will be conducted for each of the main environmental protection
targets.
1.9 Assessment factors
According to the "Specifications Concerning EIA for Highway Construction
Project  and the analysis of the pollution caused by the highway project, the main
assessment factors for the EIA are as follows.
(1) Acoustic environment: equivalent A noise level LAeq;
(2) Ambient air: TSP, bitumen smoke in construction phase; NOx, CO in
operation phase;
(3) Water environment: pH, CODcr, Petrol oil. SS.



1.8 Assessment standard

by Jiangxi Provincial Environment Protection Bureau as well as the requirements by
the World Bank environmental experts, the following standards are to be used for the
EIA:

surface water quality assessment, Class III Standard of the GHZB 1-1999  "Surface
Water Quality Standard" shall be applied ; for SS, Class I standard of the GB5084-
92  "Farmland Irrigation Water Quality Standard, shall be applied (see Table 1-3);
and for service area sewage, Class I Standard of the GB8978-1996 "Sewage
Discharge Standard" is to be applied ( see Table 1-4).

Chapter 2. Project Overview
2.1 Significance of the Project
(1) To meet the need of connection of the mid and lower reach areas of the
Yangtze river and the special economic zones of southern China
To connect the Yangtze river- the golden water channel in China and the
Shanghai-Chengdu expressways along the Yangtze river with those in Guangdong,
Hong Kong and Macao region, to strengthen the economic relations between the
economic zones in the Yangtze river delta area and the Pear river delta area, to
increase the radiant influence of the southern China coastal area, Hong Kong and
Macao region on the eastern and central China, and to further develop the economic
and cultural exchanges between Jiangxi, Guangdong, Hainan and  the regions
mentioned above, it is necessary to construct the Gan-Yue expressway.
(2) To integrate the national trunk road network system
As parts of the north-south corridor within Jiangxi province. the sections of
Jiujiang-Nanchang (Houtian), Nanchang (Houtian)-Zhangshu have been completed.
with Zhangshu-Changfu section still under construction. The road section of the
proposed highway will be the "bottle neck" of the north-south corridor if it is not to
be built right away.
(3) To meet the increasing traffic demand
The existing national highway 105 is characteristic of large traffic volume.
passing through many townships. with frequent traffic accident. The average annual
growth rate of the traffic volume on the national highway 105 is high up to 15%. with
that of some sections saturated or over saturated. To meet with the increasing traffic
demand, it is necessary to speed up the highway construction.
(4) To meet the needs of the provincial economic development
The proposed highway area is the old revolutionary base area. economically
underdeveloped. The proposed highway project will provide important infrastructure
conditions for the area to get the support from the economically developed areas in the
northern part of the Jiangxi province and the Guangdong coastal areas and will greatly
help the area' s economic development.
(5) The relations with "Jing-Jiu" railway and national highway 105
The proposed highway is located on the western bank of the Ganjiang river, and
the "Jing-Jiu" railway is located on the eastern bank of the Ganjiang river. which
forms the north-south transport network where highway transport is an important
mode between Jiangxi and Guangdong.
(6) In conformity with the overall transport development program of the Jiangxi
province
The proposed highway is an essential part of the backbone transport system in a



shape of "great cross (+)", as planned by the Jiangxi province.
(7) To meet the needs of speeding up the development of provincial tourism
resources
The proposed highway area is rich in tourism resources, with pleasant weather;
and there are not only revolutionary historical sites but also beautiful landscape and
cultural relics. Construction of the proposed highway will speed up and promote the
development of the six tourism areas of Lushan, Boyanghu, Nanchang, Jinggangshan,
Ganzhou, and Sanbaishan along the "Jing-Jiu" route area.
2.2 The Alignment Programs
2.2.1 Recommended program
The proposed expressway starts from the end point of the Changfu-Taihe section
- Mashi township (the intersection point with the national highway 105). and ends at
the Longling Town of Nankang city intersected with highway 105 (or 323). The
alignment bypasses Mashi of Taihe, Shaokou of Wan' an, Lutian, Luotang, guijiang,
Liangbizhou of Suichuan county. Qingshi, Taiping of Nankang city, Hengshi,
Mashuang, Shibatang. Neichaoyu and Longling, etc.
Figure 2-2-1 and 2-2-2 show the geographical location and the alignment of the
highway.
2.2.2 The partial alternative schemes
In addition to the recommended scheme for the proposed expresswav. there are
other six alternative schemes.
(1) Taihe Alternative I: starts from Nanyuanlong of Taihe, bypassing the northern
Wushan, via Taihe to Changwan, Dongtang, Changxi, and meets with the
recommended alignment scheme ( Scheme II ) at Xiaoshantang of Wan' an.
(2) Wan' an Alternative Il: starts from K172+500, alignment strike smoothly
along the river, bypassing Caoxia and Dutang.
(3) Suichuan Alternative Il: starts from Mantian of Suichuan county. via Tankou,
Hongshan. Xiatiandong. Xiaokan. and meets with the Alternative I at Yejiapai.
(4) Fuziling Alternative 1: located at west of Fuziling, starts from K204+638.
occupying Jinshi-Maji old road, goes around the mountain through the valley.
bypasses on the way Maji. Daopeng. Maoxia, Jiezhi, Xizhai, Zhangfang. Paiboshan of
Jinshi township of Suichuan county. via Xiaoshanheng- Fuziling vallev area. meets
with Alternative II at Leigongheng.
(5) Mashuang Alternative I: starts from Hexikou of Mashuang township of
Nankang city. via Xiagongqian, Chenkengli. Futou, along the valley area.

2.4 Brief of Engineering Works
2.4.1 Subgrade and drainage protection
(1) Cross-section of the subgrade
The width of the subgrade is 26.0m, with cross-section being composed of 0.75m
(earth  shoulder) +  2.25m  (hard  shoulder) +  0.75  (marginal strip) +  2 X 3.75m
(carriageway) + 0.75m (marginal strip) + 2.Om (median) + 0.75m (marginal strip) + 2
X 3.75m (carriageway) +0.75m (marginal strip) + 2.25m (hard shoulder) + 0.75m
(earth shoulder). The cross fall of the carriageway and the hard shoulder shall be 2%
and that of the earth shoulder shall be 4%. The standard cross-section of the subgrade
is shown in Figure 2-4-1.
(2) Subgrade side slope
The filling side slope will be 1:1.5. When it is higher than 8m, the side slope
below the height of 8m shall be 1:1.75. with l.5m side slope lane to be set in the
middle. For cutting section. the side slope shall be based on the geological
information, with such protection measures as grass planting, geo-grid side slope
protection, guard wall, earth retaining wall and etc. to be selected.
(3) Drainage and protection
0( Pavement drainage
(a) the cutting section: pavement run-off will be discharged into the side ditch.
(b) the filling section: if the subgrade slope grade large than 6m. concentrated
drainage shall be taken for pavement run-off by setting gully at the road strip;
while the slope grade is less than 6m. pavement run-off will be discharged
by the slope.
(c) Super-elevation section: a drainage system consisting of cutoff basin,
horizontal drainage pipe and gully
(d) Central separation belt: it consisting of bitumen cloth water sealing at the
bottom, vertical drainage pipes and cutoff basin
02 Subgrade drainage:
(a) Side ditch: side ditches with mortar stone pitching and ladder-type section

(b) Intercepting ditch and platform ditch: for cut sections where runoff goes to
the subgrade slop, 0.5 X 0.5m intercepting ditch with mortar pitching shall be set at
place over 5m from the outstretched area.
(c) Drainage ditch: drainage ditches will be set along the rainy road area for flood
discharge as well as for irrigation.
(Æ Protection engineering
10cm thick of unsifted crushed stone layer will be used to strengthen the earth
shoulder. For some cutting sections with soft rock or weathered stone areas mortar
pitching will be used for protection. When there are ponds, reservoir and flood area
close to the filling slope section, for subgrade slope which is 0.5m below the design
water level, then concrete pre-structure or mortar pitching will be used for subgrade
slope protection; the common subgrade are to be protected by grass planting. For
higher subgrade, mortar pitching grid stone slop protection will be adopted. To protect
subgrade slope from occupying river pass, foot slope contraction, shoulder or
embankment retaining wall will be built as restrained by the landform and land
produce, etc.
2.4.2 Bridge and culverts
The medium and large bridges are evenly distributed along the route with proper
increased number of bridge spans to improve flood discharge capacity of the bridges
and culverts. Underpasses and grade separation will be provided for sections close to
villages, with some having dual functions of drainage and passageway The bridge
scheme recommended is shown in Table 2-4-1. Based on the ground base, the bridge
will adopt spread foundation and pile foundation, which adopts cast-in-place pile.

2.4.3 Tunnel
(1) Yanggongshan tunnel: the north part starts from Yanggucun of Bizhou
I,.



township in Suichuan county, extending to the south Xiawangcun of Jinshi township
bvpassing through Yanggongshan. The tunnel is divided into left line totaling 1 560m
in length and right line totaling 1560 in length.
(2) Fuziling tunnel: located at the Fuziling mountain of Jinshi township in
Suichuan county. the north part starts from Shangxicun of Jinshi towship in Suichuan

into left line totaling 1 780m in length and right line totaling 1760 in length.

(2) Grade separation
Grade separation are built to overpass railway. classified highways or township
roads. Some grade separations are also built at some village roads (farming roads)
considering the long-term development. There are 53 grade separation in total along
the expressway and a total of 328 passageways at village /township roads and some
important field farming roads.
2.4.5 Connection road
There are three connecting roads as Wan' an . Suichuan and Ganzhou, of which.
Ganzhou road connecting the main line and Ganzhou region is very large in traffic
volume, thus adopting 1 7m wide subgrade; the subgrade width for the rest two adopt
1 2m. To put into the play of the expressway as soon as possible. the connecting roads
will be designed. constructed and completed simultaneously with the main line.
2.4.6 Road construction material along the line
(1) Quarry site
The area is rich in road construction materials with about 20 quarries for option.
The stone materials dominated by sand stone, granite stone and lime stone are of good
and hard quality. Transportation is very convenient. The main quarry sites along the
proposed road area include Wangjiaping and Majiagang in Taihe county;
Taigongshan in Wan' an county; Zhongtuan, Huangkeng and Zhuping in Suichuan
county; Zengkeng, Bazai. Dongpai. Huanglong. Tianzidi in Nankang city.
(2) Sand and gravel sites
I.?



There are about 12 sand and gravel sites for choice. The major sites include
Dukou of Shaokou township in Wan' an county, Yangcuba of Quanjiang in Suichuan
county, Shatian of Jinshi township, Luowen, Zhuping, Saxi, Shangyoujiang,
Zhangjiang, etc.
(3) Quick lime
The proposed expressway area is short of quick lime material, with only one lime
kiln each at Huanggang in Taihe county and at Kengkou in Suichuan county
respectively. It is far away from the proposed expressway and the output is low.
(4) Earth borrowing (waste) sites
Though priority has given to vertical hauling and balanced earth and stone work
in the preliminary design, but some earth borrowing and waste sites will still have to
be selected. Based on the principle of max utilization, least wastes, rational and
economical use of land, the borrowing sites are identified at some non-economic areas
as waste slope and high banks; while waste bank are defined at waste valley and lower
ground. About 11 earth borrowing and 23 waste sites are selected. for which design
has been done in respects of drainage, protection and planting.
2.4.7 Resettlement plan
RAP is required for this project and now the draft RAP has been completed.

2.6 Cost estimation and construction time schedule
2.6.1 Cost estimation
-  Funding for the proposed expressway is to be from the World Bank loan. grant in
aid from the MOC and the Jiangxi province. Total cost for the proposed project
(excluding connecting roads) is estimated at RMB 3.562.723638 million. of which
US$ 200 million are from the World Bank loan. The average cost is RMB27.795698
million per kilometer.
2.6.2 Construction time schedule
Construction of the proposed project will start in Nov. 2001 and completed for
traffic in February 2005, totaling 40 months.






Chapter 3. Overview of Environment Condition
and Current Status Assessment
3.1 Natural environment
3.1.1 Geographical position
The Taihe-Ganzhou section of the Gan-Yue expressway passes by the four
counties of Taihe, Wan' an, Suichuan, Ganxian, and two cities of Ganzhou and
Nankang, all the way through the southern hinterland of the Jiangxi province in north-
south direction. It is located at 25040, -26∞50, N and 114050,   115000,
3.1.2 Landform
The alignment of the proposed expressway is from the north to the south, along
the Ganjiang river towards the upper-stream direction. The landform of the whole area
is characteristic of high in the north and low in the south. The route starts from the
Jietai basin area, going through Suichuan, Nankang hilly lands, and ends at the river
valley area of Shangyoujiang river and Zhangjiang river in Lishan of Nankang.
The road section of Mashi (Taihe)-Luomukeng (Nankang) at the start point is in
a hilly area. where the landform has great topographical relief with steep mountains
and widespread gullies and with elevation over 250 - 550; and the section of
Luomukeng-Lijiashan at the end point (Nankang) is in a light hilly area, with
alluvial plain in the valley of Shangyoujiang river and Zhangjiang river. where the
landform has gentle undulation widely developed with class II river terrace with
elevation over 90--150m.
3.1.3 Geological condition and earthquake
(1) Lithological character and geological structure
Great differences exist in terms of lithological character along the highway route
area with outcropped strata.
The geological structure is dominated by old strata developed with broken ground
in north-east direction from the southern Suichuan to the northern Nankang. with
locally outcropped direct folding.
(2) Hydrological geology
There are four types of underground water classified by its source, storage
manner and hydraulic features, i.e. carbonate fissured cavern water, carbonate tramp
detrital cavern fissure flow, detrital rock fissure flow, and detrital rock fissure pore



w ater.
(3) Poor geological condition
The route covers various geological and landform areas. The in-situ investigation
shows that the poor geological conditions possibly encountered in the construction
process mainly including karst, cave, and intermontane liman soft ground.
(4) Neotectonic movement and earthquake
The neotectonic movement in this area is developed continuously based on the
previous tectonic movement. characteristic of succession and intermittency, with great
areas intermittent uplift activities. The differential mobility between fracture tectonic
and block fault is not conspicuous with less earthquake activity.
The earthquake intensity in the area is less than six degree, according to the
",Seismic Zoning Map of the People' s Republic of China" (Jiangxi Province,
1990); therefore earthquake resistant may not be considered for the bridge. tunnel and
other structure design.
3.1.4 Hydrology
The route is along the west bank of the Ganjiang river from the north to the south
in upper stream direction. crossing over Suichuanjiang river, Zhangjiang river and its
branches. The rivers passed through bv the route include Shushuihe, Suichuanjiang,
Shangyoujiang and Zhangjiang. which belong to the Ganjiang river system, flowing
into the Boyang lake. The main source of their run-off flow comes from rainfall,
mostly concentrated through April and June with great fluctuation of the flow volume
from season to season. Floods usually happen over April-July with peak flood in
Mav and June and duration of the flood over 15-20 days.
The frequencies of calculated water levels for each of the hydrological stations
are shown in Table 3-1-1. Suichuanjiang and Shangyoujiang are navigable with
planned navigation channel of Class VI: with no navigation requirement for other
rivers.
Table 3-1-1 Frequencies of the water levels
Frequency       Xiaxi (Suichuanj iang  Yaoxia (Zhangshui)   Tiantou (Shangeoujiang)
1I%O               84.64                123.45              121.42
5%                 83.84                121.78               119.54
Data source from the Feasibilit\ Stud% Report of Gan-Yue Expresswav (Taihe-Ganzhou Section) b% JPCDI. Dec.. 1999.



3.1.5 Meteorological condition
The area passed by the proposed expressway is belong to subtropical monsoon
climate, characteristic of cold winter and spring, hot summer and dry autumn. more
rainfall in summer, dry and cloudy in Autumn with less sunshine and long period of
frost-free. It is rich in thermal resources and abundant rainfall unevenly distributed
across the year.
(1) Temperature
The annual average temperature in the whole area is over 17.7C - 19.20C; with
the highest in summer through July and August, monthly average temperature over
26.6∞C -29.8∞C; the lowest in winter through January and February, monthly average
over 3.50C-6.60C; the annual extreme highest up to 400C -40.47C and the annual
extreme lowest down to -6.640C - -9.9640C; annual average frost-free period over
281 -286 days, the longest of 335 days and shortest of 249 days.
(2) Rainfall
The annual precipitation of the area is over 1.372- 1.595 mm. with the maximum
over 1,877-2.102 mm and the minimum of 823 mm. The rainfall over March -
June is 762 mm, accounting for 50% of the year; that over July-October 396 mm.
accounting for 27% of the year; that from November to the next February 396 mm.
accounting for 27% of the year. There are average of 157 rainy days, with the
maximum of 202 days and the minimum of 111 days and the longest continuous rainy
period is 26 days.
Owing to the unevenly distributed rainfall across the year. usually flood first
followed by dry season in the growing period of double-cropping paddy. The annual
precipitation usually tends to increase with the increase of the altitude.
(3) Wind direction and speed
In summer. the subtropic high pressure dominates with most wind coming from
the south; in the other seasons of spring, autumn and winter, it is dominated by
continent high pressure with most wind coming from the north, owing to the north-
south direction of the Ganjiang river valley.
Annual average wind speed is 1.9m/s. with monthly average over 1.6-2.3m/s.
3.2 Ecological environment
3.2.1 Current status assessment of fauna and flora
The area is located in the mid Asia sub-tropic zone and the flora belong to eastern

3.2.3 Current status investigation of agricultural crops
The area has warm weather with nice hydrothermal conditions. The main
agricultural products are paddy rice. bean etc.. main cash crops are cotton, sugar cane,

3.2.4 Current status of soil erosion
3.2.4.1 Factors to cause the soil erosion
The soil erosion in the area along the proposed expressway is higher than the
provincial average except for Suichuan county. The main factors to cause the soil
erosion are rainfall. landform, parent soil quality. cover plants, and human activities.
The landform in the proposed expressway area is of various type dominated by
hillv land accounting for over 70% of the total, which is vulnerable to soil erosion.
The annual rainfall is unevenly distributed in terms of season, March-June rainfall in
form of heavy rain or storm accounts for 55 percent of the whole year. in which the
big rain erosion leads to the heavy wash of the surface soil which takes up 75 percent
of the whole year, thus resulting in heavy soil erosion.
The red soil accounting for 60 percent of the soil in this area is weak in anti-

Cover vegetation is the critical factor in defending soil erosion. Due to long-time

agricultural means are actively used to improve the ecological condition. Soil erosion
has been mitigated to some extend. From Table 3-2-3, the most sections along the
route are medium and below soil erosion area, only the places closing to destination
are heavy soil erosion areas.

belong to the Yangtze river system, with its east source Gongjiang river, west source

Suichuan river is the fourth branch of the Ganjiang river located at the main stream of

is 162 km and the perennial average runoff is 2.894 million cubic meters.

effective irrigation areas of 296,400 ha. and 290,100 ha., accounting for 77.8% and
81.1% of the total farmland area in Ganzhou and Ji' an respectively.
The investigation showed that there is no water intake from drinking water
resource for the river sections within the assessment area. The main drinking water
sources come from underground water.
3.3.2 Monitoring and assessment of the water quality status
To understand the water quality of the main rivers. some river sections are
selected for water quality monitoring. One cross section monitoring is set at the bridge
site for each river section, surface water is taken once a day for two days running at
10m from both riverbanks where a vertical line is set at the river center. The sample
analysis method will follow   " Environmental Monitoring Analysis Method, . The
monitoring and assessment results are presented in Table-3-3-2.

3.4 Assessment of Acoustic environment
3.4.1 Current acoustic status and sensitive location survey
Most sections of the proposed expressway are located in mountain and rural areas,
where the current environmental is rather quiet without any large noise source. Since
some of the resident areas are beside the existing road and its intersection, there are
some noises affecting the resident areas. The main noise in the village comes from
living and fowls, cries. After consulting the preliminary design documents and site
reconnaissance. the sensitive spots of resident quarters and schools in the assessment
areas of the proposed expressway are presented in Table 3-4-1-lTable 3-4-3 .

3.4.2 Current status monitoring and assessment
Acoustic environment status monitoring shall be carried out for the representative
sensitive spots defined in the TOR ( as shown in Table 3-4-5 and Figure 3-4-1). The
monitoring instruments, method and frequency are in accordance with the
specifications  set  forth  in   GB   /  T14623-93    "Urban   Area  Ambient  Noise
Measurement Methods" . The monitoring results are presented in Table 3-4-5 which
shows that:
(1) The current status of noise level measured at the resident spots along the
proposed expressway area are: daytime Leq 41.6"-55.7 dB; nighttime Leq 34.3'-49.7
dB. most of the resident areas meet the Class I or even Class 0 standard. except for a
few  village exceeding the Class I limit but still up to the Class II standard, which
indicate a good acoustic environment.
(2) The current status of noise level measured at the sensitive spots of school and
clinics are: daytime Leq 41.2-53.9 dB; nighttime Leq 40.9-45.1 dB. meet the Class
I standard.
(3) The monitoring results show that the current status as a whole of the acoustic
environment along the proposed expressway area is good.

3.5 Assessment of ambient air
3.5.1 Current status
The alignment of the proposed expressway has been arranged away from the
large sensitive spots of urban and township areas, with most areas passed through by
the highway are rural and wild areas, where the air quality is kept in natural conditions.
There is no large fixed pollution source along the proposed expressway area. The
existing air pollutants mainly come from the emissions from highway traffic,
secondary flying dust. CO and TSP from daily life: but the discharged volume is
small. Therefore the current status of the air quality along the proposed expressway is
good.
27



3.5.2 Monitoring of current status
Following the principle of "points representing the line" , some typical
sensitive spots have been selected for monitoring the status of the ambient air quality.
(  The items to be monitored are TSP, and NOx.

carried out as to ensure 18-hour valid data; for TSP, 12 hours/day (6:00-
18:00), filter paper once in the morning and once in the afternoon;
(E) The sampling analysis method shall be in accordance with the specifications
set forth by the NEPA. The current status monitoring and results are
presented in Table 3-5-1

impact on the areas along the proposed expressway. The project area has defined six
directly influenced and 9 indirectly influenced. In which, the directly influenced areas
include Ji' an prefecture (Taihe. Wan' an. Suichuan), Ganzhou prefecture (Ganxian,
Ganzhou  municipality. Nankang); the  indirectly  influenced  areas are  Yongxin.
Jinmgangshan. Ji' an county. Xinguo, Yudu. Shangyou. Dayu, Chongyi and Xinfeng.

3.6.2 Outline of the social economic conditions in the direct influenced areas
(1) Areas' economic conditions
The proposed expressway area has solid industrial strength, especially the
electricity, machinery, chemical and textile industries play an important part role in
the province.
The Ji' an region has established an industry system including the electronic
industrv mainly  with electronic machine. electronic elements. electric wires and
cables: the medical chemical industry mainly with medicines and camphor: the food
industry mainlv with fruit, milk, sugar, wine: and the building materials industry
mainlv with cement. granite, marbles. finishing materials.
The Ganzhou region has established an industry system including metallurgical,
electric. coal, chemical. machine. electronic. forest, building materials, food, light
industry, textile industry. etc.. with over 3,000 enterprises. There are also national
non-ferrous metal and rare-earth metal production bases; and the provincial industrial
production bases of sugar. paper manufacturing. wood-based plate. cigarette. forest
product and chemical products.

(2) Agriculture
The Ji' an region is located in the Ganzhong plain area, with rich and fertile land.
abundant resources and excellent agricultural production conditions. The agricultural
product output in 1998 reached RMB 9,479 million (current price), with growth rate
of 2.7% over the previous year and 1.5 times higher than that in 1990. The township
enterprises are thriving and become the major force in the rural area, s economy. The
main farm products are increasing steadily, of which the grain product output reached
2.662 million ton in 1998. an increase of 2.84% over the previous year.
(3) Commerce and trade
For Ji' an and Ganzhou total value of domestic retail sales of commodities
reached RMB 6,367 million and RMB 7,755 million respectively in 1998, 38.87%
and 11.2%  up respectively over the previous year. The market is developing rapidly
together with the development of the tertiary industrv of service industry, banking.
tourism and information industry. which is becoming a pillar of the national economy.

3.6.4 Current status of transport infrastructures
(1) A profile of transport network
The transport facilities in Jiangxi province are under developed. with 2.125km
railwavs. 35.234km highway. 4.937 km inland waterway. There are three main
corridors in the province. i.e. 3 railway lines of Beijing-JiuJiang railway. Zhe-Gan
railwav and Wan-Gan railway: 3 highways of national highway No. 105. 206 and 320:
and 2 waterways of Ganjiang river and XinJiang river. The whole transport system in
Jiangxi province includes railway. highway. watenvay. civil aviation. and pipeline.

I> Current status of railway
In Jiangxi province there are six trunkl railways of Zhe-Gan. Ying-Xia, Wan-Gan,
Jing-Jiu. Xiang-Jiu and Wu-Jiu and eleven branches inside or passing through Jiangxi
province. with railway mileage in operation of 2,175km.
Jing-Jiu (Beijing-Jiulong) railway is an important part of the Gan-Yue transport
corridor. The Gan-Yue railway section starts from north Shahejie of JiuJiang city,
passing through Nanchang, Ji' an, Taihe., Ganzhou, Dingnan, and the Guangdong
province' s Longchuan, Huizhou, Shenzhen, and end at Jiulong, with total length of
1,070km. of which 700km are in Jiangxi province and 370km are in Guangdong
province.
According to the statistics, the passenger transport volume by Jing-Jiu railway
reached 4.3 million in 1998. increasing by 32.3% over the previous year; the freight
volume dispatched reached 4.489 million in 1998 an crease of 31.7% over the
previous year. Rapid increase of passenger traffic and the large capacity of the trunk
railway put great pressures on the provincial railway sections. The Xiangtangxi-
Ji' an section' s availability ratio has reached 93.3%; that of the Ganzhoueast-
Longchuan section reached 109%. which is over loaded.
, Current status of highway
The Gan-Yue highway is an important part of Jiangyxi-Guangdong corridor. and
also the important component of the backbone highwav system in the shape of
,-cross f '-J . also one of the economic trunk lines in Jiangxi province. At present.
most of the 243km expressway have completed and open to traffic beyond the north
of Changfu: and the traffic on the section beyond the south of Changfu is over the
capacity. with some sections very serious. As the result. the highway is congested
w ith service level decreasing and with frequent traffic accident. Therefore more
highway capacitv and higher service level are needed for Jiangxi province.
t%3 Current status of Ganjiang waterway
Ganjiang river is the second large branch river of the Yangtze river and the
number one large river in Jiangxi province from south to north. an important
component of the north south transport corridor in parallel with Jing-Jiu railway and
the national highwvay 105. Owing to a number factors the navigation conditions of
Ganjiang river was deteriorating, with great amount of cargo turned to highway and
railwvay since the Jin(g-Jiu railway starting operation in 1996. The waterwav transport
is in a difficult time for further development.

) Mineral resource
There are rich mineral resources in Ji' an region. with a total about 50 kinds of
mines discovered. of which there are 85 sites with proved reserves.
The Ganzhou region is also rich in mineral resources. with reputation of abundant
rare metals and known as one of the important non-ferrous metal production bases and
known as the ,Capital of tungsten" of the world and the -. Kingdom of Rare
soil . There are a total of 99 kinds of mines having been discovered. 33 of which
have proven reserves. In addition to tungsten and rare soil. radioactive mineral
products are ranked in the top place in the country.
j Tourism
Jii an has rich tourism resources. such as the beautiful scenic mountains of
Jinggangshan. Qingyuanshan. Yuchishan; and there are nine national level
revolutionary and cultural relics units in the area. Jinggangshan was described as the
- "No.l mountain in the world"  by the famous general Zhude. where there are not
only cgreat amount of historical sites. but also charming landscape. listed as one of the
i forts best tourist attractions"  in 1992. In the area there are 60 scenic spots. 270
culture and historic sites. There are also temples of Jingjusi. Jiezhou Kiln. Bailuzhou
Shuvuan. Wentianxiang Tomb. Xiyanggong. Large Scale Tomb of Shang Dynasty,
Relics of Grain Storage of Zhanguo (the Warring State). and etc..
The area of Gannan (southern Ganzhou) is rich in natural and cultural resources,
32



including the natural beauties of Danxia terrain and Karst hills and lakes. such as
Cuiweifeng, Yushiyan, Meiling, Luotianyan, Hanxianyan, Niedu Karst, Tushui Lake,
Wudnagshan with 99 different peaks, the 300 hills of East River source area, and etc..
In the area there are 17 national level cultural relics sites, 48 provincial level cultural
relics sites, 94 county level cultural relics sites. The famous national historic city of
Ganzhou has typical cultural relics of Song dynasty. There were 32,602 tourists from
overseas visited Ganzhou in 1998, increased by 554 persons, with tourism income of
USD 7.68 million, increased by 17.79%.
The above mentioned scenic spots are far away more than tens of kilometers from
the proposed expressway and not in the assessment area.
(3) Water engineering facilities
By the end of 1997, there were a total of 1,225 reservoirs with total capacity of
4.116.97 million m3; irrigation facilities of 10,965: irrigation stations of 608; effective
irrigation area 12.4 ha..
(4) Post and telecommunications
The post and telecommunications are developing rapidly. By the end of 1998. the
total out put value of post and communications service reached RMB 3.990.471
million, increased by 44.8% over the previous year; the household telephone terminal
of 1.18 million. increased bv 26.66% over the previous year; mobile telephone of
240.900; the internet user of 771. increased by 4.3 times over the previous year. The
telephone ownership in Jiangxi province is 5.9 per hundred persons.
In the rural and township areas the post and telecommunications are also
developing rapidly. By the end of 1998. the telephone user in rural area reached
465.000.
(5) Urban and township lavout and planning
The Tankou township in Ganzhou is an important urban area along the proposed
expressway. beyond the south of the Fenggang township. is the planned area for an
airport. the area beyond the south of Longlingxiang is belong to the planned area of
Nankang city. The proposed expresswav is 2km away from the airpor and 2km away
from Tankou development zone. The alignment selection has avoided these areas.

and Mitigation Measures
4.1 Assessment of Ecological Environmental Impact
4.1.1 Land occupation' s impact on land utilization
The proposed highway (main line) intends to take up a land surface of 11,218.8 mu,
of which paddy field accounting for 37.9%, followed by wood lands accounting for
30.4%. In terms of the jurisdictional composition of the land occupied. Nankang has the
largest proportion accounting for 52.7%. followed by Wan' an accounting for 22.0%.
The land occupation is illustrated in Table 4-1 -1.

35



acute contradiction of less land and large population. and will aggravate the pressure on
the remaining agricultural fields, thus exerting some impact on agricultural production
and land utilization. Although the land size being occupied by the road only accounts for
a tiny part among the total land of the directly influenced area, but in terms of the local
land contractors, it will exert relatively great impact on them. Highway land occupation
will exert a short-term impact on the income of the farmners along the road whose land has
been occupied.
Similarly, the temporary land occupation during the construction stage will also
produce some negative impact on local agricultural cultivation. But compared to
permanent land occupation, the size of temporary land occupation is relatively small and
they can be virtually restored by clearing and reclaiming. So the adverse impact of
temporary land occupation during construction stage on land utilization and economy is
temporary.

To sum up. the land occupation by this project will exert some impact on the local
land utilization and agricultural ecology. But the construction of this expressway will
u reatly improve the transportation infrastructure required by agricultural cultivation and
processing. thus promoting the rural economy of the Ganzhou prefecture into a higher
level by materializing the value of land resources in utilization.
4.1.2 Impact on fauna and flora along the expressway
Most of the flora to be damaged by the expressway construction is agricultural crops.
planted woods and wild bush. of which the expressway w-ill take up a total of paddy fields.
drv lands and woodlands with a size of 8.512.2 mu.
As there is neither primitive forest nor endangered tree species along the road. the
expresswvay construction will not produce long-terrm destructive impact on vegetation.
36



The employer as well as the proposed construction unit will strictly follow the
planting design specifications and requirements issued by the Ministry of
Communications. This will not only compensate for and restore partial original
vegetation damaged by construction to some degree, but also protect the subgrade, reduce
soil erosion, flying dust and mitigate the traffic noise.
Most of the animals living in the assessment area are domesticated animals, fowls
and a few common wild animals that are not particular with their habitat environment. but
are relatively adaptable to human activity. In this case the proposed highway will not
cause significant change to their habitat environment nor interfere with their normal life.
They can still survive in the area along the road.

The location for earth borrowing and waste areas will be selected locally from the
nearest location and restore the fields. The earth borrowing pits will be mainly located
in non-commercial areas as waste hills. waste slopes. desolate valley and low-productive
farmlands. The earth borrowing and waste areas. after being leveling and clearing. can be
used for agricultural infrastructure construction. the deep-cut section can be developed
into paddy fields or fish ponds so as to increase the utilitv of land value. Therefore the
selection of the pits is relatively reasonable. During the construction stage. the earth
borrowing pits should be leveled, reclaimed and replanted from time to time so as to
restore one pit after it is finished so as to restore its ecological condition. This work and
responsibilities shall be specifies and implemented in the contract between the employer
and the contractors. When the borrowing and waste areas are to be used for farming. the
top cultivate soil taken from the farmland occupied by subgrade can be used to cover the
pits.
Environmental protection engineering has been designed for the borrowing and
v, aste areas for this project, including drainage ditch. mortar pitching slope. planting trees
and grass. etc. The adverse impact can be controlled so long as the earth borrowing and
waste disposal are conducted strictly in accordance with the design and the environmental
protection works.
4.1.4 Forecast and analysis of soil erosion impact
39



(1) Forecast of soil erosion intensity during construction
The intensity of soil erosion depends on the rainfall, the condition of covering plants,
gradient, etc. The soil erosion intensity is forecasted based on the soil erosion equation by
taking into considerations and quantifying the differences before and after the
construction work. The forecasting model is as follows.
E=R *K  Ls *C *P
wihere: E;-Erosion intensity (t/km2 *a);
R - Erosive factor of rainfall,
K - Soilfactor, 0.42 -0.46for loose soil in road engineering:
Ls - Terrain factor, a function of surface run-off length and gradient,
calculated by the follows:
A
Ls =(  -m* -(65 Jsin2 O + 4.56sinO + 0. 065}
22.1
where.  A - Length of eroded slope (m):
9- Gradient of eroded slope;
m - Experience index:
C - Surface coverage factor;
P - Soil r etention measures factor.
It can be seen from the above equation. that the soil erosion intensity is mainly
related with such factors as rainfall (R factor), soil quality (K factor). terrain (Ls factor).
cover plants (C factor) and management (P factor).
R: represents dynamic factor of water erosion. related with rainfall volume and
intensity. constant before and after construction.
K: is the sensitivity of soil to the erosion, related with granularity and organic content
in soil. Farmland soil usually has fine granular structure and medium permeability. with
K < 0.4. For soil underneath the cutting areas' surface. the soil structure is most likely
of block or laminated structure. with medium/slow permeability and with K over 0.42-
0.46: in construction staoe K = 0.45. depending on engineering geological conditions.
Ls- A is the lenoth of slope: before construction. A = 50m; after construction the
average subgrade filling depth is 3.5m. the length of slope from pavement to water
drainage ditch is A=6.31m. 0 is the gradient of the slope: before construction. 0=10'; after
construction the 0=340. m is experience factor. before construction when 0=10∞. m=0.5:
and after construction. when 0=34'. m=0.8.
The results of the calculation show that before construction Ls = 4.253; during
40



construction stage. Ls = 8.454.
C: is the coverage factor, depending on the type and coverage rate of cover plant;
usually depending on land use, Table 4-1-7 and 4-1-8 show the C values under different
conditions; before construction work, average value of C=0.5; during the construction
stage, the cover plants being denuded, C=1.0.
P: is the soil retention measures factor, taking into account of the effects of such
measures as leveling, compacting, building check dam or sediment dam; the P values
under different conditions are shown in Table 4-1-9. Before construction, most area along
the road are farm land and wood land, which can be seen as smooth ground through
leveling and tamping, the P=0.7; during construction stage. the construction site is rough
irregular ground caused by bulldozers, the P=1.0.

Drainage and protection engineering measures will be taken based on the geological

The drainage engineering works for this project includes pavement drainage and
subgrade drainage. The protection works include retaining wall. protection wall, side
slope and grass planting. etc. The purpose of these drainage and protection works is to
protect the stability of the road subgrade and road slope, as well as to reduce rainfall' s
washing of the slope and to reduce soil erosion produced from road construction so as to
conserve water and soil. These protection works will be carried out simultaneously with
or in advance to the subgrade construction (such as the retaining wall) and will be
inspected and accepted simultaneously with the subgrade. Also, in the later period of
construction, the covering vegetation will be recovered on the earth side slope with some
planted turf which will reduce soil erosion of the side slope. Though the soil erosion will
be increased in the initial construction stage (the first or second year). but it will be
gradually reduced later on and be under control in the year of completion and acceptance.
thus the soil erosion will be much less than that in the initial construction year.
From the comprehensive analysis of the protection and plantation engineering. we
can see that as long as the protection measures can be finalized, the soil erosion caused by
the expressway construction can be controlled.
43



(4) Analysis of soil erosion impact during operation stage
At the beginning of the operation stage, the covering plants such as grass and bush on
most of the side slopes may not be fully recovered; and later on, along with further
planting measures to be carried out, the vegetation coverage in the side slope will be
increased year by year. Although soil erosion may still exist, it will be in a small quantity
and under direct control. It is estimated that after 2 -3 years in the operation stage, the
soil erosion caused by the expressway will be under effective control, with soil
conservation for the project related areas up to the level before construction or even
better.
4.2 Water Environmental Impact Assessment
4.2.1 Construction stage
(1) Sewage from large-sized construction camp
Large-sized bridge construction is characterized of long construction time.
concentrated and stable construction work force, the sewage from the construction camp
may easily be discharged into rivers.
The construction work time for bridge is set to be 23 days/month. According to bridge
construction volume and similar bridge' s construction, 80,000 working days are needed
for Shushuihe bridge with an average of 150 workers on site each day: for Suichuanjiang
extra-large bridge. 180,000 working days are needed with an average of 300 workers on
site each day; for Shangyoujiang bridge,130,000 working days are needed with an
averaoe of 250 workers on site each day; for Zhangjiang bridge, 80,000 working days are
needed with an average of 150 workers on site each day. In southern China, given that
each person consumes an average daily water volume of 90 L and that the sewage
discharge factor takes 0.8. the sewage discharged from the construction camp can be
calculated by the following formula, with the calculation results shown in Table 4-2-1.
Q5 = (k -ql - Nj)/1,000
where: Qs - discharged sewage volume (t/d):
k- discharge/fcctor (0. 6 -0. 9) in service area, here it is 0.8:
-    qI - discharged sewage quota (L/person - day);
Nl - number of people.
The sewage discharged from the construction camp may have negative impact on the
surrounding environment: therefore it is recommended that the sewage be treated by
septic tank before it is discharged.
44



Table 4-2-1 Estimated sewage discharge from bridge construction camp of Gan-Yue expressway
construction site  Shushuihe bridge  Suichuanjiang bridge  Shan)oujiang bridge  Zhangjiang bridge
Discharged sewage t/d)  10 8          21 6            18 2             10 8
Mlain pollutants  SS    BOD5     CODcr    TOC        TN        TP     Organ c P
Concentration (mg/L)    55  110     230      80        20                 l
(2) Impact on the downstream river water quality by bridge construction
Due to the construction of bridge pier or cofferdam in the initial construction stage,
there will be silts and sand suspensions excavated from the river bed. In the construction
of pier. boring cast-in-place concrete pile will be adopted by use of cofferdam, which can
separate the water inside the cofferdam from the river water; therefore the silts and
suspensions arising from boring operation will have little impact on the river water
quality. The most likely impact caused by the bridge construction may come from boring
wastes in great amount, which should be discharged into designated place as selected
with consultation with relevant local authorities, such as the EPB and water engineering
bureau. The discharge process of the wastes should be supervised by environrnental
protection supervisor to reduce the negative impact of the wastes on the water quality and
the flood discharge as far as possible.
(3) Impact on water quality caused by construction vessels
The vessels used for bridge construction are usually small in size (no more than
90Kw), the sewage and the waste water discharged would be one ton per day for each
ship. The vessel wastewater is mainly cabin washing water and bilge water which
contains sand mixed with some oil and rust. however they would be sedimented quickly
after sometime. The bilge water is a mixture of leaked water from different valves. oils
and fuel from different machines. with an annual average volume of 10% in the total
loading capacity. The wastes content discharged from the ship mav be complicated and
wili exert negative impact on the water quality of the water body.
4.2.2 Operation stage
- (1) Impact on the surrounding water body from pavement run-off
The pavement run-off flow produced by rainfall may be calculated by the following
formula:
W=AXhxlO-3
where: W  - pavement run-off per unit length (m3/d),;
A  -  subgrade width (m).'
h - rainfall intensity (mm/d).

It can be seen from the above equation that, the pavement run-off flow depends on
the rainfall. The proposed highway area' s annual average precipitation is 1,494.8mm;
and the Ji' an region' s annual average precipitation is 1,487mm. The pavement run-off
produced in the rainy season can be calculated and summarized in Table 4-2-2.

The pollutants carried by the run-off in rainy season mainly are SS and oil, mostly
happened in the initial rainfall period. The flow speed of the rivers as Shushuihe.
Suichuanjiang, Shangyoujiang, Zhangjiang, Ganjiang is stable with great dilution
capacity. There is no centralized drinking water intake in the assessment area downstream
the bridge site; therefore the impact of the bridge pavement run-off on the water quality
of the rivers is not significant.
(2) The impact on the existing agricultural irrigation system
There is an integrated agricultural irrigation system in the proposed project area with
relatively good infrastructure. Existing water channels will cross over the proposed
highway by way of small bridges and culverts. The feasibility study report shows that
there are total of 14 small bridges with a total length of 391.53m  and 482 culverts
included in the recommended scheme; in the alternative scheme there are a total of 22
small bridges with a total length of 659.61m and 455 culverts. Flood discharge and
irrigation functions have been taken into full account in the design of the bridges and
culverts. as well as convenience of local people' s production and daily life. Proper
modification. combination and connection have been arranged in the engineering design
for the existing channels and ditches. including restoration of the malfunction ditches and
connection of dead end channels; therefore the highway construction will have little
negative impact on the agricultural irrigation system.
46



4.2.3 Water pollution estimation for service area
The proposed project intends to service areas in Suichuan (K195+900) and in
.anzhou (K259+500), occupying a size of 51 .870m2 and 40,000m2 respectively.
The wastewater discharged from the service area, mostly living sewage and auto
washing water, can be calculated by the following formula.
Qs = (k -ql -N1)/1 000
Qq = (q2 - A2) / 1, 000
where: Qs -   discharged sewage volume (t/d)
Qq -   discharged auto washing water volume (t/d);
k  -  sewage discharge factor (0. 6 -0. 9) in service area, here it is 0. 9,
ql-   discharged sewage quota per each person (L/person - day);
Nj-  number ofpeople.
N2 -   number of washed vehicle (veh./day):
q2-   wvater volume needed to wash a vehicle (L/veh.)
Based on the experience of the existing expressway service area, given the number of
people in the service area being 200 (including staff member and passengers), the average
water consumption being 90 L/person per day. then the daily sewage volume will be 16.2
tons for the service area.
The number of vehicles to be washed is estimated at 2% of the forecasted traffic
volume, with the water needed per vehicle being 400L/veh.; then the vehicle washing
wastewater produced from the service area in the initial, mid-term and long-term

C  The noise level on the highway construction work site will be high, since more

exert a relatively small impact at places I OOm away, and will exert relatively great impact
on people nearby the construction site(within50m), particularly at night time, such noise
will affect their sleep. Schools, hospitals and residences 50m within the center line of the
road will suffer from big impact from construction noise. therefore the construction time
should be properly arranged to avoid construction in school time and people' s sleep
time. If it is impossible to arrange. temporary mitigation measures shall be taken..
X Large construction machine and the electricity generator with high noise level
will have serious impact on the operator' s health. particularly the impact on the
operator' s hearing ability. Statistics shows that noise deafness is not only related with
the sound level. but also with the time exposed to the noise. The danger of noise can
induce other illness. So. these large machines' noise can exert a big impact on operators
and nearby residents. In road section with sensitive locations such as school, clinics, the
use of high noise construction machine should be avoided and the construction work time
48



hould be properly arranged.

Based on the above mentioned calculation formulas and parameters. the traffic noise
forecast for the proposed expressway (main line) in the operation stage can be made as
listed in Table 4-3-3. In the light of the Class IV standard under the GB3096-93. the areas

(I ) By the standard of Class IV under the GB3096-93 ( i.e. the day time noise level
limit of 70dB and the night time noise level limit of 55dB). the daytime noise at two sides
of the expressway during operation stage can meet the standard; the nighttime noise is
excessive at 60m away from the road in the initial operation stage and it will increase
with traffic volume. and will be excessive at I OOm away in the long term operation stage.
(2) Although traffic noise in daytime is not excessive. and the traffic noise at night
can meet standard I OOm away from the road. the operation of this expressway will lead to
an obvious increase of noise over the current status, so its interference with residents
cannot be neglected.

4.3.3 Ambient noise forecast and assessment for the sensitive locations
The ambient noise forecast for sensitive locations should be modified by taking the
around surface conditions, embankment or cutting height, limited road length into
consideration. The ambient noise should be added with background noise. with iteration
formula as follows.
(LAeq)forecast=1 Olg[]O l (LAe&traffic+10 0. l(L Aebackground]
The forecasted noise value and the excess over the standard limits by the above
formula and by their respective acoustic environment are listed in Table 4-3-5 -Table 4-
1-7.
It can be seen from Table 4-3-5 that:
(1) In the long-term operation stage, the daytime traffic noise excess will be more
than 6.7dB for Wan' an Gongda university. since the university has been moved away
wtith no more teaching activities and habitants in it, therefore. there will be no traffic
noise impact.
(2) The daytime traffic noise excess will be 9.9-13.1dB. 9.3-12.6dB and 10.5-
13.6dB for Zhuhu Primary School. Mashuang High School and Qiubian Primarv School
respectively. which will have serious impact on the school teaching activities. Therefore
environmental protection measures should be taken. Although the nighttime noise level is
high. there is no teaching and residing in the school at night. so the impact is not big.
(3) The daytime traffic noise excess will be 5.7-9.9dB and that of nighttime will be
9. 3  12.8dB for the Kangfucun and the Nankang Skin clinic. which indicates that
effective measures should be taken to mitigate the noise impact in the operation stage.
(4) The daytime traffic noise excess will be 0.8-2.6dB for Wuling High School.
Ho-owever. the teaching building is a bit far away and is perpendicular to the road. the
impact on the school teaching is not great. As for Daping Olds, home. the daytime
traffic noise will be exceeding by 2.7-7.Odb and that at nighttime is 6.8-9.8dB which
shall have great noise impact, but it is very small and could be removed 200m away
from the road.

4.4 Ambient air impact forecast and assessment
4.4.1 Construction stage
The air pollution in the construction stage is mainly caused by secondary flying dust
arising from the mixing plant, the vehicles and road construction machine operation on
the construction site. Therefore the assessment factor is the TSP for the construction
stage.
(1) Dust pollution from stabilizer
Stationary mixing plant technology is to be used for the expressway construction.
According to the on-the-spot monitoring at the Bazhou mixing plant for the Jin-Bao
(Tianjin-Baoding) highway project conducted by the MOC Research Institute of Highway.
the TSP concentration at place 50m in the leeward direction away from the mixing plant
was 1 .367mg/m3, which exceeds the Class II Standard limit: while the TSP concentration
at place 100m in the leeward direction away from the mixing plant was 0.61 9mg/m3.
Since the area is located in mid Asia subtropic monsoon climate zone with humid air and
high humidity; the ambient TSP concentration will be less than that at the Bazhou mixing
plant for the Jin-Bao highway.
(2) TSP arising from construction and hauling vehicles
In the construction stage, the transportation and loading/unloading of the building
materials at the construction site will produce TSP pollution. Field monitoring of TSP
produced by vehicle transportation in similar construction site shows that the TSP
concentration at place 1 50m from the roadside usually exceeds the Class II standard limit.
which indicates that the TSP arising from the transportation may cause serious pollution.
(3) The air pollution impact caused by bitumen pavement construction
Bitumen pavement will be constructed for the expressway. Bitumen smoke will be
produced by bitumen melting and mixing, which will have certain impact on the ambient
air quality. According to the on-the-spot monitoring of the bitumen smoke at the
Dayangfang bitumen mixing plant in Beijing by RIOH. if advanced mixing plant such as
the Italy made MV,A is used. the bitumen smoke concentration at place 100m in the
leeward direction away from the mixing plant will meet the standard requirement as
specified in GB 16297-96 ,Comprehensive Air Pollutants Emission Standard" . If
ordinary bitumen melting and mixing equipment were used on the construction site. the
bitumen smoke concentration would greatly exceed the standard limit. Therefore. the
mixing plant shall not be located within 300m in the leeward direction where there are
sensitive locations, such as hospitals. schools and residences.
62



4.4.2 Operation stage
4.4.2.1 Meteorological analysis
(1) Climate features
The project area belongs to mid Asia sub tropic hilly area and monsoon climate,
characteristic of cold winter and spring, hot summer and dry autumn, rainy season in
beginning of summer, cloudy and dry autumn with less sunshine and long frost-free
period. There are abundant thermal resources with great temperature difference and
plentv of rainfall unevenly distributed. Historical annual average temperature is 17.7-
19.2∞C, annual average precipitation is over 1.434.3mm'-1,457.5mm, with rainy season
from April through June.
(2) Ground wind
D Wind direction: According to the last three years conventional meteorological
statistics provided by the National Meteorological Center, the N wind prevails in Taihe
county with frequency of 11%: ENE wind prevails in Suichuan county with frequency of
12∞%: NNE wind in Ganzhou with frequency of 14%. followed by NE. NNW (9%).
NE(I 1%) and N(9%). Table 4-4-1 -Table 4-4-3 show the statistics of wind direction and
frequency statistics of each county and city. Figure 4-4-1 -4-4-3 show their wind
direction rose maps.
2 Static wind: is the wind with speed less than 1.0rm/s. Under the condition of static
wind it is not good for air pollutants to be dispersed, particularly when the static wind
occurs concurrently with inverse temperature. which is easy to result in serious air
pollution. The static wind frequencies for the three areas are 22%. 23% and 34%
respectively. Summer and autumn have the highest frequency of static wind.
.D3 Wind speed: is an important factor in determining the dispersion and dilution of
the pollutants in the air. Table 4-4-1-4-4-3 show the wind speeds in the three areas. The
annual average wind speed is 2.4m/s in Taihe. I.9m/s in Suichuan and 2.0m/s in Ganzhou.
Suichun has the lowest wind speed with relative poor pollutant dispersion conditions.
AA Pollution coefficient
To estimate the extent of air pollution it is necessary to take into consideration the
v nmd direction frequency and the average wind speed. The pollution co-efficient is
defined as follows:
Cp =fi / Vi
where:    Cp    average pollution coefficient.
fi -frequency of wrind direction;
Vi    average wZind speed in a direction.
63



The calculation results are listed in Table 4-4-1-4-4-3. and illustrated in Figure 4-4-
4 -4-4-6.
The greater the pollution coefficient in a direction, the more serious of the pollution
extent will be in the leeward of the direction. It can be seen from Figure 4-4-4-4-4-6
that the directions with the highest pollution coefficient for Taihe, Suichuan and Ganzhou
are ESE, WSW and NNE respectively.
(3) Determination of the air stability
According to the observation by the meteorological department. the air stability along
the project area is dominated by category D followed by category E-F.

4.4.2.2 Calculation of vehicle emission pollutant source intensity
In the operation stage, the air pollutants will mainly come from vehicle tail gas,
which will be in proportion to the traffic volume and will also be related with vehicle
tvpe and vehicle operation mode.
(1) Traffic volume forecast
The traffic volume forecast and the composition of the vehicles are the same as those
mentioned above.
(2) Pollutant source intensity calculation
The pollutant source intensity can be calculated by the following formula:
3
Qj = 2A i . Eij / 3600-1
,=,
wi,here. 0  -  typej gaseous pollutant source intensity (mg/s a m);
Ai    hourly traffic volume of type i vehicle in forecast year (veh./h):
Eij-  under motorway conditions, individual vehicle emission factor for
pollutant jfrom i type vehicle in forecast year (to adopt the value as recommended by the
"Specifications for Environmental Impact Assessment of Highway Construction
Project - ), mg / veh. * m.
The calculation formula for the peak hour pollutant source intensity is as follows:
QIX. = QL   AG
where: AG -  peak hour traffic volume coefficient, here it is 6.2%.
The calculation formula for daily axverage pollutant source intensity is as follows:
QC,=QL  A,/R
where. Ar -  daytime traffic volume co-efficient, Ar = 84.8%for the expresswvay.
R - day time hour, here it isl 6.

4.4.2.5 Pollutant compliance in each road section
(1) It can be seen from  Table 4-4-4  that NOx  concentration at place 23m   from  the
road center will meet the Class 11 standard limit under category D air stability even in the
72



long-term operation stage. but Nox could exceed the standard limit at place within 23m.
(2) Under unfavorable weather conditions (static wind, low speed wind, inverse
temperature) or frequent ups and downs in the road with complicated landform, so that
the pollutants are not easy to be dispersed. then the NOx concentration at place 23m from
the road center will exceed the standard limit.
(3) According to the forecast, the CO concentration from the vehicle emission will be
very small in each section. And there is no large-sized stationary CO pollutant sources
along the road, so the CO background concentration is also low. Therefore the CO
concentration along the line will meet the assessment standard required.
(4) Impact analysis on sensitive locations
X  After the resettlement, all the sensitive locations will be all beyond 23m away
from the road center and are beyond NOx and CO concentration excessive scope,
therefore the concentrations of NOx and CO for all the sensitive locations will meet the
Class II standard limit.
1) For the sensitive locations 30m within the road center at the Ganzhou-Tankou
section (with high traffic volume) and Suizhou-Tangcun section (complicated landform).
their NOx concentrations of leeward the perennial prevailing wind direction may exceed
the Class II standard limit under unfavorable weather conditions.
4.4.3 Assessment of air pollution in tunnel
This project has designed two single-direction and dual-hole tunnels in
Yan-gongshan and Fuziling, the former tunnel is 1 560m long in its left route and 1 560m
in its right route. the latter tunnel is 1700m in its left route and 1720m long in its right
route respectively.
The hazardous substances in the tunnel air mainly come from the CO, NOx.
hydrocarbon. S02. aldehyde and carbon particles, which are poisonous to the human
body.
According the energy conservation law of pollutants in the tunnel, the forecasting
mode for the poisonous gas concentration in tunnel is:
.Q   . *A
S*U
W1here  C-polluitant concentration at a certain cross-section in the tunnel. mg/m3;
Q-pollutant discharging souirce intensity, mg/s. in;
X-distanceffrom a certain cross-section to the ent-ance. in.
S-surface of the tunnel cross-section, m2;
U-airflowr speed within the tunnel, m/s.
73



The air flow speed within single-direction tunnel depends on the vehicle, s piston function
:riving in the tunnel. which will not exceed 5m/s according to experience. If ventilation machine is
used. the air speed can be increased. In this circulation, the wind speed is set to be 5 m/s. and the
ross-sectional surface (S)of the tunnel is set to be 5 1 .25m.

When there is traffic jam within the tunnel, the vehicles and the wind speed will greatly reduce,
rhe CO and NOx concentrations will increase by many times and are difficult to disperse. thus causing
narm to human body. In addition, the fume and other particles emitted from diesel engines can greatly
reduce the visibility within the tunnel, affecting the driving safety and human health. So when the
tunnel is over lOOOm long. it is very necessary to install ventilation machine.
4.5 Assessment of Social Environmental Impact
4.5.1 Population distribution
The completion of the proposed expressway will have certain impact on the
population distribution along the project area. The expressway will greatly improve the
road capacity. pavement conditions and reduce traffic accident, and the improved
transport capacity will promote industrial and commercial development along the area,
particularly around the interchange area with newly developed small townships,
business centers as well as the increased people from outside : therefore there will be
certain effect on demography and population density.
Since the resettlement will be arranged locally. the local population will have no
great changes in the townships and villages along the line.
4.5.2 Indirect impact analysis for the proposed project
( I)Indirect benefit analysis
The congestion of the existing national highway 105 is 0.72-1.74. It is estimated that
almost all road sections will be saturated or over saturated by year 2003. meanwhile with
the urbanization of the highway 105 and the increased density of population, traffic
accident happen s frequently. Table 4-5-1 presents the accident statistics of highway 105
within Ji' an and Ganzhou territory as well as that for Chan-Jiu expressway. It can be
seen from the table that though traffic volume on the expressway is obviously higher than
that on the lower-grade highways, yet the accident ratio and the loss arisen is much lower
than that of the lower-grade highways. In addition to this. the expressway brings more
indirect benefits by saving transport cost. time.etc. which is summarized in Table 4-5-2
