(2) Energy saving analysis of the project
9 Energy saved from the up-graded highway
The implementation of this project will upgrade the highway into expressway that
'ill save the petrol consumption. According to the survey. the average vehicle speed of
the existing highway 105 is 45kmlh,consuming 42.7 kl/100 vehicle-km (calculated by
PCU). if with the expressway, it can save 12.3kI/I00 vehicle-km. The proposed
.xpressway totaling 128.4454 in length will save 454.000kL fuel daily if calculated at
76



weighted average for normal daily traffic volume of 28706 vehicles within the assessment
time horizon.
C2 Energy saving from shorten mileage
The proposed project will shorten the driving mileage by 38.6156km. Based on the
traffic survey and its forecast results (calculated by transferred traffic), it can save about
331 .OOOkL fuel daily if calculated at weighted average for daily transferred traffic volume
of 20094 vehicles within the assessment time horizon.
03 Energy saving analysis
The proposed project is a full access control, interchange expressway with design
speed of I OOkm/h. The speed-up vehicles will shorten the transport time and reduce the
unit cost. It can save about it can save 12.3kl/100 vehiclekm, based on this, the
recommended scheme will save average fuel of 785,000kl daily.
4.5.3 Economic features, industrial structures and labor force
Completion of the proposed highway will promote the local area, s economic
development with newly emerged industry and labor force, as well as inter-regional
economic exchanges to improve the local area' s investment environment.
It can be expected that after completion of the proposed highway the electronic
industry. medical and chemical industry, metallurgical industry. paper manufacturing.
tobacco industry, food industry and building materials industry will be developing faster.
Meanwhile  the  commerce,  catering,  banking.  building  industry. transport.
telecommunications and information industry will also have conspicuous growth.
The completion of the proposed highway will give impetus to the urban development
along the highway to promote the land use and resource development so to make the
industrial structures more reasonable. Around the expressway and the connection road
there will be developed into an industrial and commercial belt.
The industrial development and the improvement of the investment environment will
create more employment opportunities for people from both the urban and rural areas and
more people will move from rural area into the urban area with more people working in
the tertiary industry.
4.5.4 Transport
The national highway from Tongjiang-Sanya is located in the coastal areas of Fujian
and Zhejiang provinces, and the national highway of Beijing-Zhuhai is located in middle
of China. The Gan-Yue expressway is located between the said two national highways
and is the most convenient corridor to Shenzhen and Hong Kong; therefore the
77



.ompletion of the Gan-Yue expressway will integrate the national highway system.
The proposed highway is part of the Gan-Yue expressway -- the north-south corridor
in Jiangxi province, with its alignment roughly in parallel with the national highway 105.
the Ganjiang river and the Jing-Jiu railway. It connects the golden water of Yangtze river
and the Jiujiang-Jindezhen special motorway in the north; links the Zhe-Gan railway, the
national highway of Shanghai-Ruili, the national highway of Beijing-Fuzhou, the national
highway 308. 316 in the hinterland; and connects the national highway of 319 and 323 in
the south. The proposed highway will attract most of the through traffic from the existing
national highway 105 and part of the intra-province traffic. It will ease the traffic
congestion on the national highway 105 and will play an important role in facilitating
links between the railways and the highways as well as the freight and passenger traffic.
which is essential to the integration of the transport system. The.proposed highway will
connect the existing 11 provincial and local county and rural roads, forming an effective
road network to promote the areas' economic development.
4.5.5 Land acquisition impact analysis
The proposed expressway is located mostly in hilly and mountainous areas. where
cultivated land is very precious. In the alignment selection full consideration has been
Oiven to occupy less farmland as much as possible for the proposed highway. Total land
occupation of the expressway is 11218.8 mu. of which 4.393.33mu are paddy fields.
1.067.20mu are dry land. 4.534.28 mu are wood land. with paddy field area accounting
for over 35.0% in the total. Additionally, the temporary land occupation is 1.194.77mu
for the expressway.
The project land occupation is permanent which will loss its original productivity and
inevitably have certain impact on the area' s agriculture and forestrv. However. the great
economic and social benefits brought about by the project will eventually transform the
land use. greatly increase and materialize the land value. Land use pattern will greatly
change with newly emerged industrial zone and more land for industrial use. To avoid
loss of precious cultivated land resource, it is recommended that the land administration
department should strengthen management over land use along the project area.
The land acquisition for the proposed project will make some of the farmers lose their
land. becoming surplus labor. National land compensation policy will be implemented for
the proposed project. The local village board will develop collectively owned tertiar;
industry to provide employment opportunitv for those who lose their land. They will have
the priority to get employed for the construction of the proposed expressway to solve
their short-term  income shortage. which will mitigate the impact arising fiom  land
78



acquisition.
4.5.6 Living standards (Rational analysis on the convenience, interchange and
passageway provision)
Due to the full access control of expressway. the villages and farmland on both sides
of the road will be separated. which will cause inconvenience to local people' s
production and daily life. A total of 53 separated grade crossing and 328 passageways
have been provided with an average of 2.9 per every kilometer to accommodate the
layout of the existing local roads. Therefore, the convenience of the local people' s life
will not seriously affected.
4.5.7 Removal and Resettlement
A total of 1 29.335.0m2 buildings are to be removed, and a total 51 .330m of power&
telecommunications facilities are to be relocated.
The basic principles of the resettlement policy are as follows.
(1) Compensation shall be made to the resettled households to ensure that the
building area and quality of the resettled house will be up to the original ones: and the
compensation will be carried out before commencement of the road construction so as to
ensure their living and economic rights.
(2) The newly built houses for resettlement will be arranged at one side awa) from
the road for the purpose of convenience for farming and community life.
(3) For villages with large resettlement volume, house-building plan shall be made to
reduce farmland occupation as much as possible; and multi-story building may be built
when it is necessarv.
(4) To solicit individual household' s opinion one by one on resettlement and to
listen to their requests, to make them satisfied as much as possible so as to ensure that
their living standards will not be lowered after the resettlement.
The owner of the highway project attaches great importance to the resettlement and is
formulating the resettlement action plan (RAP) and a supervision agency has been hired
to-supervise the implementation of the RAP. Corresponding coordination agencies have
also been set up at the county. township and village level concerned with the land
acquisition and resettlement to carry out the land acquisition and resettlement policy and
to strictly follow the RAP. Therefore the negative impact caused by the resettlement may
be reduced to the minimum. Meanwhile precautions will be taken not to occupy farmland
and to avoid other environmental impacts caused by the resettlement.
79



4.5.8 Harmony of highway and landscape
The newly built expressway is away from the urban area, with most of the sections in
n'illy and mountainous areas with different terrain and landscape. Planting beautification
is included in the design to be in harmony with the landscape by plantation of suitable
bushes and flowers. Along the highway, some flower and bush shall be planted to show
the elegance and magnificence of the expressway, thus it will not damage the original
natural landscape. but can symbolize the beauty of modem expressways.
Different type of side slope protections such as the diamond shaped and arch type
slope protections may be selected for plantation to make the expressway a green corridor.
Beautification of large expressway structures such as the interchanges and bridges
may restore the damaged natural landscape caused by the construction and can improve
the tour environment to form a new expressway landscape along with the natural scenery
and cultural landscape..
4.5.9 Impact on local community and local infrastructures
With the completion of the proposed expressway and its promotion to the local
economic development, there will be a rapid increase in the demand for post and
communications. power and water supply, education, medical service, etc.. The demand
mav not be met by enough supplv in a short term, but in the long run will stimulate the
supply and promote the improvement of the areas public facilities.
4.5.10. Impact on the cultural relics and historical sites
According to the ,Cultural Relics Survey Report (Third Version) of Gan-Yue
Expressway (Taihe-Ganzhou Section)", provided by the Jiangxi Provincial Cultural
Relics Archaeological Institute (JPCRAI) in December,2000. the cultural relics along the
proposed project area are of protection at county and municipal authority, which are listed
in Table 4-5-3 and Figure 4-5-1
According to the Survey Report. the above mentioned cultural relics and historical
sites are distant away from the proposed expressway with nearest of 0.7 km and the rest
alL distant from the road by more than 1.0-3.0 km. so they will not impacted by the
expressway construction.
However. because ancient relics are deeply buried, most of them are not found and
identified. According to news report. there are Cretaceous period strata widely distributed
in Nankang city area, and it is very likely to find dinosaur eggs fossil and bone fossil in
cutting and earth borrowing. Therefor. the JPCRB and the JPCRARI have selected 10
spots along the Nankang section to excavate for trial. The result of the excavation

4.6.2 Probability estimation of dangerous cargo transport pollution risk analysis
The traffic accident probability estimation is based on the existing traffic accident
number. road traffic volume, dangerous cargo transportation volume and the proposed
highway' s sensitive length. The traffic accident number of the proposed highway or its
sensitive sections is estimated by the following formula:

Although the accident probability of dangerous cargo transportation is very small,
but if happened. the consequence can be very serious. If happened on large bridge, it is
likely to damage the bridge structure and to leak hazardous substances such as cyanide.
pesticide, petroleum, sulfur acid into the river. thus polluting the river water. If happened
within the tunnel. it can cause traffic jam or even fire or explosion, very harmful to the
safety of drivers and passengers.
Therefore, great emphasis should be given to the risk of transporting hazardous
cargo. It is required that road administrative department should make a good emergency
plan and should enhance its accident handling abilitv through training and management
so to minimize the pollution risk (further refer to the contents of counter-Measures).
4.7 Environmental Impact from Building Materials Excavation, Transport and Its
Mitigation Measures
The building materials will be mainly transported by vehicles. The distribution and
transportation conditions of the quarries refer to Table 4-7-1.

(1)   Impact on existing road transportation
The sand and gravel required by this project will be self-excavated along the road or
purchased from outside, generally be transported by rural roads or detour roads to the
construction site, not by major roads such as the National Highway 105. In addition,
cement, timber, steel and bitumen will be transported by the National Highway 105. Due
to the heavy traffic of major roads in this region which already exceeds their design
capacity, the transportation of building materials may lead to traffic jams and affect
traffic safety to existing roads. During construction. traffic management over existing
roads must be enhanced such as to transport the building materials at night and in non-
busy season, to formulate transportation management plan for the project so as to ensure
the transportation requirements of the building materials.
(2)   Ecological damage
Stone is mainly cut by boring and explosion. Large stone mine is exploded, crushed.
classified and finally sent to the construction site. New construction of detour roads and
stone excavation will damage the existing surface vegetation and will change partial
landform, resulting in new soil erosion and disharmony with surrounding landscape.
(3)   Impact on residents' living quality
Excavation and transportation of stone w-ill produce flying dust. noise. shock.
explosive danger and traffic jam, etc.
The stone quarries for this project are all located in waste hills with large stone
reserve and far from towns, villages and schools. The flying dust, noise, shock and
explosive danger produced from stone excavation will not impact residents, living. but
attention must be paid to the health and safety of the operators.
When transporting on existing roads, the building materials may exert some impact
on local residents' living and schooling along the roads. Road flyIing dust and material
spill due to bad covering will have some adverse impact on people' s living environment.
esp. in dry seasons.
In addition. transportation of building materials may aggravate the traffic pressure
on existing roads, resulting in traffic jams. which can make people inconvenient to travel
and increase traffic accidents.
To mitigate these impacts, the following measures can be taken:
(i) Quarry contractors must adhere to the safety regulations concerning outdoors
xplosion. Explosion time should be set to avoid rush hours so as to protect workers'
iafetv. Contractors must adhere to relevant labor protection regulations to provide
84



helmets and earplugs to workers and provide periodic physical examination to them.
(ii) Soil erosion and vegetation loss caused by quarry can be minimized by
enhancing management and by stipulating excavation plan.
(iii)   Transporting vehicles should adhere to local traffic rules, overloading is
forbidden so as not to cause spill of bulky stone or other materials and not to cause traffic
jams.
(iv)   Construction detour roads should be sprayed with water periodically.
Vehicles hauling bulky building materials shall be covered by cloth.
(v) Contractors shall prepare a good transportation plan to avoid peak hours.
(vi)   Routes to transport stones shall be reasonably selected so as to avoid dense
residences and schools as far as possible. If large residence exists 50m within the route,
then the transportation should be not allowed at night (22:00-6:00). Alsomexplosion is
forbidden at night.
(vii)  In daytime. if transportation causes noise interference to schools and
residences near the detour roads. then mobile sound barriers can be used to mitigate the
noise impact.
(viii) Transportation management over the National Highway 105 should be
enhanced. Contractors are required to well maintain their vehicles so to make their noise
level to a minimum.
(ix)   Supervisory engineer is required to enhance noise monitoring. If the
transportation of building materials does make the acoustic environment of residences
along the existing roads (105) deteriorating. the route may be considered for a change or
some economic compensation may be made to local residents.
4.8 Environmental Impact Mitigation Measures
4.8.1 Design stage
4.8.1.1 Ecological impact
(1) To further optimize and adjust the alignrnent. to reduce occupation of cultivated
Cields. to reduce the volume of earth disposal and the quantities of earth borrowing and
w-aste areas.
(2) The construction camp shall be located away from agricultural fields as far as
possible. Construction scheme shall be reasonably arranged so to reduce the time of
temporary land occupation.
(3) The planting works and the main body of the road should be carried out
synchronically. Priority should be given to local species of arbor, bush and grass so as to
restore and compensate for the vegetation.
85



(4) Drainage and protection engineering work should be designed for the subgrade,
ncluding intercepting ditch, side ditch, protection wall, side slope, retaining wall,
Drotection gird. which can not only stabilize subgrade. but also prevent soil erosion.
(5) Mashuang Bridge is located in a geologically complicated section. Geological
-econnaissance should be enhanced in the design of the construction drawing, and side
;lope treatment program will be designed.
(6) The south exit of Yanggongshan tunnel faces a valley between two hills; a viaduct
.vill be built here to avoid high fill and valley realignment.
(7) Environmental protection will be designed for the 26 earth borrowing pits and the
20 waste areas.
4.8.1.2 Water pollution
(1) Drainage engineering will be designed so that the pavement run-off will not be
Airectlv discharged into sensitive water body.
(2) Water canals or ponds occupied or separated by subgrade will be re-built or newly
quilt.
(3) Sewage treatment is designed for service areas so that the sewage can meet
iational standard.
4.8.1.3 Noise impact and ambient air pollution
According to forecasting, during the construction stage. sound barriers, relocation.
nstallation of soundproof windows will be carried out for different sensitive. locations.
.hich will be included into the design and tendering documents.
Stone quarry, earth borrowing and waste area. and mixing plant will be located 300m
tway from residences. The hauling route for building materials will be rationally
lesioned so to avoid residences as far away as possible and to avoid flying dust and
ioise.
l.8.1.4 Cultural protection
We entrusted the Jiangxi Provincial Cultural Relics Bureau and Jiangxi Provincial
ultural Relics Protection Institute to make surveillance along the road. They have
tubrnitted the report. Refer to the Report of Cultural Surveillance for details.
1.8.1.5 Resettlement
The design for this project has always emphasized to avoid towns, less removal and
and occupation. A hierarchy of resettlement offices will be set up to formulate RAP. The
86



Jiangxi Normal University Institute of City and Population is employed as an
independent supervisor. Details refer to the RAP.
4.8.1.6 Public participation
In the alignment of the road, setting of interchanges, environmental protection,
resettlement, we have consulted with along-the-road governments, concerned
departments. non-governmental organizations, rural committees, collectives and even
individuals to solicit their opinions so as to gain support from the public.
4.8.2 Construction stage
4.8.2.1 Ecological impact
(1) To enhance workers' awareness of environmental protection of natural resources
and not to damage wild life and not to cut trees.
(2) Sewage and garbage from construction camp shall be collectively treated or
made into family fertilizers.
(3) Earth borrowing and waste disposal shall be conducted strictly in accordance with
design requirements so to well protect and restore the surrounding environment. The top
soil (30cm) of the acquired land shall be kept for reclaiming and compensation.
(4) Construction vehicles shall run in detour roads, not in agricultural fields nor
woodlands.
4.8.2.2 Water and soil conservation
(1) Engineering measures
< To reduce the area and number of construction sites as much as possible.
Construction should be carried out within designed site: the earth borrowing and waste
area should not be enlarged casually so as to reduce the exposed area of cutting. Don' t
enter to the site so earlier if construction is not ready.
4, For road sections with deep cutting/filling (such as the section of K192+900-
K199-660.547. K221+000 - K260+000). the engineering measures such as earth
retaining wall. protection wall. concrete anchoring should be taken combined with side
slope plantation of grass to make it stable and to prevent sliding. Terrace should be
arranged for deep cutting section: intercepting ditch shall be set 5m away from the top cut
area to discharge the run-off from the top surface of the side slope.
4) The various protection engineering works should be built concurrently with the
major works (as seen in the design drawing of subgrade protection and planting design)
so as to prevent side slope soil erosion caused by pavement run-off.
87



(j)When it is raining, sand bag or straw mat may be used to cover the slope surface to
reduce soil erosion; earth excavation for bridge or culvert should be avoided in rainy
season.
5) In the process of the wastes disposal, stratified compaction should be made based
on the height of earth retaining wall so as to reduce the gradient of slope.
(©)Water drainage ditch and intercepting ditch should be built for the earth borrowing
sites to reduce rainfall eroding force; the earth borrowing site should be flat as much as
possible after the borrowing. If the borrowing is to be made from a site with big slope,
check dam and sediment control dam should be built together with proper drainage
system.
(2) Planting Measures
X Planting should be carried out in accordance with the design requirements.
X The turf selected for the slope when planting and covering in a lump sum should
have the following features: fast growing and fully covering the ground surface; strong
bonding force with the soil to prevent surface soil erosion: perennial plant in harmony
with the environment.
3 To get the best effect. the side slope plantation should be completed one month in
advance to the rainy season.
(3) Land Reclaiming
1) Reclaiming and planting measures should be taken after completion of the
oorrowing and disposal sites to prevent soil erosion by rainfall.
g2 For the waste bank in hilly areas, forestation is the major means. Grass. bush and
irbor with deep and flourishing roots capable of withstand harsh conditions should be
selected for the forestation so to ensure the plantation coverage rate up to 50% in the
second year.
1  For the waste bank nearby the farmland, agricultural reclaiming should be
,onsidered. It may be planted with herb after first being leveled and soil improved; and
awricultural crops may be planted when the soil is fertile.
i The deep cutting areas may be built into reservoir or fish pond: and some waste
;ites may be used as for resettlement building or industrial building area.
4.8.2.3 Water pollution
OCentralized treatment shall be done for machine oil pollutant from construction
machines; solid wastes with machine oil should be stacked at designated place in stead of
88



-hrowing away casually.
Æ2Septic tank and garbage tank should be provided at the construction camp for
:imely cleaning of the wastes; building materials should be stored with rainfall proof
-overing protection.
(Dn the section of cultivated fields and water ponds, the drainage ditches at the two
'ide of subgrade shall be heightened and solidified to prevent mud entering.
(A)Sand sediment tank shall be set up in construction site near river or reservoir to
prevent mud from directly entering into water body.
4.8.2.4 Noise pollution
(1) When the construction site is close to school, no construction work with heavy
noise machines should be arranged at school time: when the construction site is close to
densely populated residence, construction work with strong noise machines should not be
arranged at nighttime.
(2) To use construction machines with low noise level as much as possible. For
-onstruction machines with high noise level, temporary sound barrier should be adopted
Lo mitigate the noise impact. The construction materials storage site and the mixing
plant should be located 300m away from the acoustic sensitive locations.
(3) The construction operator' s work time should be arranged in accordance with
he labor hygiene standard. and personal protection measures such as wearing ear- plugs
and helmets. etc. should be provided to the operators.
(4) The detour roads for the construction should be selected away from such sensitive
ocations as schools. residences and hospitals. When dense residences exist 50m within
detour road. transportation of building materials is forbidden in such detour road at night.
(5)The transportation of building materials may make the acoustic environment of
he residences along the existing roads (105) deteriorating, supervisory engineer is
equired to carry out noise monitoring at six locations: Gaopo (Wang' an county).
Iigongduancun (Shaokou township), Quanjiang (Suichuan county). Luowencun
Suichuan countv). Changshengcun (Fenggang township). Bazicun (Mashuang township).
According to the results. if necessary. the hauling route may be considered for a change:
f it is impossible to avoid. temporary sound barrier or some economic compensation may
*e given into consideration after consulting with the local residents.
4.8.2.5 Ambient Air Pollution
(I) The stabilized soil and bitumen mixing plants should be set up at the leeward side
300m away from the sensitive locations of residences. hospitals and schools. The mixing
89



plant should be equipped with sealing device, shock absorber and dust remover. Labour
protection measures should be provided to the operators of the construction machine such
as eve mask and mouth mask.
(2) Bulk construction materials transported by truck should be covered to prevent
spillage as much as possible.
(3) Hauling roads and construction site, particularly the stabilized soil mixing plant,
should be sprayed from time to time to prevent secondary dust flying.
(4) In the process of subgrade filling, spraying should be made according to the need
of compaction. After the compaction the contractor should spray the compacted ground
from time to time to prevent flying dust.
(5) The storage of the bulk construction materials should be covered and over 300m
away from the sensitive locations as school and village.
4.8.2.6 Traffic and transportation
( ) To ensure a smooth operation. construction detour roads must be set up at the
intersection of the expressway and other existing roads, which should be generally
located at one side of the original road and built into subgrade after the interchange is
completed.
(2) Traffic and transportation management over the National Highway 105 should be
enhanced. Passing time will be limited such as to avoid transporting building materials at
rush hours. Also contractors are required to make a good transportation plan.
(3) Materials will be prepared in advance. Sand and stone will be stored at relatively
less traffic time.
(4) Local public securitv and transportation management departments shall be well
coordinated with to mobilize traffic jam and to handle traffic accident so as to ensure a
smooth running.
(5) Contractors are required to make measures to cover the bulky materials so as to
prevent spill and leakage in transportation.
4.8.2.7 Cultural relics protection
During construction. if underground cultural relics are found. then construction
should stop and the supervisory engineer will protect the site. and concemed department
will be notified to handle it.
4.8.2.8 Worker' s health
(1 ) Septic tank and garbage tank shall be set up at construction camp. which are to be
90



cleared by the contractor periodically so to prevent outbreak of disease. Drinking water
that complies with hygiene standard shall be provided at the site.
(2) Contractors must adhere to labor protection regulations to provide helmets,
earplugs and periodic physical examination to workers.
(3) A full-time healthy work shall be available at construction camp to provide
medical security and give hygiene education to the site workers periodically.
4.8.2.9 Public participation
Complaint telephone number for environmental complain should be conspicuously
marked at the construction camp. For complaint problems, the employer and contractors
shall contact the local environmental department and such problem should be settled
within 48 hours.
4.8.2.10 Implementation of "Three Simultaneousness"
Contractor at the bid section shall implement facilities such as the sound barrier and
sewage treatment simultaneously with the main body engineering according to design
requirements.
4.8.3 Operation stage
4.8.3.1 Ecological impact
(1) Planting shall be continued in accordance with the engineering design for such
areas as side slope, central belt. interchange. service area so as to recover the vegetation.
protect the subgrade, and reduce soil erosion.
(2) To recover the damaged vegetation and ecology in time so to prevent denuded
surface. A greening belt of some width should be set up at the two sides of the road
(3) Major structures such as the extra-large bridge and the service area shall be
planned concurrently with the expressway construction by giving considerations to the
harmonyi of the landscape and the environment.
(4) The water-through culverts should be cleared in time to ensure a smooth running
of wsater in the irrigation system.
è5) The protection and greening engineering should be maintained.
4.8.3.2 Soil erosion
Further improve the soil & water conservation works. planting works. and land
reclaiming works according to design requirements. A combination of grass. flowers.
bushes. and arbors may be used to form a stereo planting pattern. In the later operation
stage. greening should be prompt so as to protect the subgrade stability and to reduce soil
91



erosion.
4.8.3.3 Water pollution
(1) The sewage treatment facility at the service area should be maintained so as to
ensure the sewage meeting discharging standard.
(2) Execute the water- quality- monitoring plan and supplementary environmental
protection measures will be taken according to the monitored results.
4.8.3.4 Noise pollution
(1) Traffic noise control
Adhered to the ,Regulations Concerning Ambient Noise Pollution Prevention and
Control of the People' s Republic of China" , strengthen the road traffic management
and road maintenance. Motor vehicles with high noise level exceeding standard limit
should be banned to drive on the road.. Table 4-8-1 shows the allowable noise level for
motor vehicles.

4.8.3.4 Ambient air pollution
(1) Management over vehicles hauling bulky materials such as coal. cement. sand and
;tone. and easily packaged fertilizers and pesticides. These vehicles should be inspected
it the expressway entrance and be covered when haulingt the above materials.
(2) Tunnel fans should be maintained to ensure good ventilation within the tunnels.
(3) Planting works should be carried out at both sides of the road, which is good to
Absorb the flying dust and to protect the ambient air quality.
(4) Ambient air monitoring plan should be implemented. supplementary
-nvironmental protection measures shall be taken according to the monitored results.
96



4.8.3.5 Solid wastes
Regulations shall be formulated and advertised to forbid passengers to throw away
cans and paper bags so as to ensure safe driving and the highway hygiene.
4.8.4 Transportation management of hazardous substances
4.8.4.1 Design phase
(1) A closed and complete drainage system will be designed to lead the bridge
pavement run-off into the subgrade drainage ditch so as to prevent leakage of hazardous
substances into the river water.
(2) At the entrance of the 9 large bridges and the 2 tunnels. "Careful Driving"
warning boards (yellow) and "Max. Speed 60km" boards (red) for dangerous cargo
vehicles will be set up respectively so to remind drivers to pay attention to safety and to
limit the speed.
(3) At lOOm in front of each toll gate entrance. a reminder board (blue) will be set up
to remind the drivers of dangerous cargo to run by side and to declare for inspection.
(4) Tunnel safety design
L To establish tunnel operation management facility and to equip with relevant
facilities
The tunnel operation management facility is composed of 8 system as ventilation.
powver and lighting. firefighting. traffic control. emergency telephone. circus TV
monitor. fire warning. central control. of which the ventilation system is composed of
jet fan. fan motor. CO monitor and visibility monitor. the firefighting system is
composed by fire cock, chemical extinguisher. the fire warning system is composed by
buttons.
The tunnel is longitudinally ventilated by jet fans. Two fans asa group equipped
with one control device. There are a total of 48 fans.
Water for firefighting comes from underground. which is lifted by a pump into a
water tank. Water is supplied by pumps.
9 An emergency parking lot will be built at a good surrounding rock in the middle
place in each of the two tunnels and one transverse gallery is set up at the relevant
position. two interval pedestrian transverse gallery will also be set up.
3, Special mark will be set up to remind drivers to pay attention to safety.
4.8.4.2 Transportation management of hazardous substances in operation phase
To ensure safety of dangerous cargo transport. laws and regulations have been
97



oromulgated, mainly as the following.
(1) "Regulations Concerning Chemical Hazardous Materials Safety Management"
.ssued by the State Council;
(2) "Rules Concerning Motor Transport Hazardous Cargo"  JT3130-88;
(3) "Measures Concerning Firearms Management of the People' s Republic of
China";
(4) "Regulations Concerning Explosive Materials of the People' s Republic of
China":
(5) "Regulations Concerning Radioactive Isotopes and Radioactive Equipment' s
Radioactivity Management of the People' s Republic of China";
(6) "Rules Concerning Hazardous Transport", issued by the Ministry of Railway;
(7)  "Measures Concerning Hazardous Cargo Transport Management . issued by
Jiangxi Provincial Highway Administration Bureau.
According to the above laws and regulations. the current management mode system
over dangerous cargo transport is as follows.
(I) The prefecture and municipal Traffic Administration Bureau (TAB) set up the
local distribution of hazardous chemicals transport and carriage agency network;
(2) To undertake hazardous cargo transport. the carriers and freight forwarders shall
make application to the local TAB to get special certificate subject to examination and
ipproval by the TAB. Those involved with hazardous cargo transport such as the
manufacturer. sale. storage. carrier. freight forwarder should report to the regional and
-municipal TAB the hazardous cargo transport plan and the details of the hazardous cargo:
(3) There  are  special   "driving  permit .   ,driver license" .  "escort"
equiremnents for the chemical hazardous cargo transport. with uniforn special signs for
he vehicles. which have to be inspected periodically: relevant personnel should be
rained and certified.
X4  The route and the parking area of the hazardous cargo transport shall be
Jesignated by the public securitv bureau (PSB) and fire fighting department. Vehicles
ransporting chemical hazardous substances should be parked at designated place
( 5) Special unified route bill is required for long distance hazardous cargo transport to
-e checked the PSB and TAB en-route. which is to be inspected and supervised by each
)LLblic security and transportation departments..
For this project. the following management will be made for hazardous substance
ransportation:
(I) Declaration system is enforced for vehicles transporting hazardous substance.
Driver needs to fill a declaration form. including certificate number of the carrier.
98



code of the hazardous cargo, names of consignor and consignee. loading and
unloading place, characters of the cargo. etc..
(2) At the entrance and exit of tunnel, the driver, s three licenses should be
inspected, and the route bill should be accepted. After safety inspection, the
cargo is allowed to go.
(3) Usually the hazardous cargo transport is arranged at off peak hours
(12:30-15:00). When the weather condition is bad it is not allowed to be on road.
(4) At the entrance of the highway, the "Safe Driving guidelines for Gan-Yue
Expressway" will be distributed to drivers, which, prepared by traffic safety
experts, includes emergency handling methods, safety committee address and
telephone.
I5) The declaration and inspection of vehicles transporting hazardous substance at
the highwa) entrance are to be made by the toll gate charger who will be trained
on the management. declaration. safety inspection. work procedure and fire
fighting. which will be incorporated into the project training plan.
(6) When the vehicles loaded with hazardous cargo as blasting cap. dynamite.etc.
will pass through the tunnel. the toll station staff shall notify in time the staff in
the tunnel who shall send specific person to escort the vehiocle(s) passing
through the tunnel.
4.8.4.3 Probabilitv analysis of security inspection for hazardous substance hauling
vehicles by tollgates
Transportation of hazardous cargo by Chinese vehicles shall adhere to the
Guidelines for Hazardous Cargo Transportation by Vehicles JT3130-88) issued by the
\linistrv of Communications. which specifies in detail the hazardous cargo' s
2 lassification. packaging and marking. vehicles and equipment. checking and
locumentation. consignment and delivery. transportation and unloading, custody and
tirefighting. supervision and management.  Vehicles hauling hazardous cargos shall be
rezlistered  in  transportation  authorities and  be subject to their supervision  and
*nanagement. Entering onto the expressway,. the vehicles shall pay to the tollgate. sign
Doard (blue) shall be set up at lOOm in front of the gate to remind drivers to drive in side
nd to activelv declare for inspection. At the outer side of the tollgate. an extra wide lane
4.2ni) shall be set aside for extra wide vehicles and hazardous cargo vehicles to run. In
iddition. the hazardous cargo v ehicles shall hang a signal flag with characters
-Hazardous Cargo" in yellow background in the front of left side to remind tollgate to
onduct safety inspection of them.

4.8.4.4 Probability analysis of accident within tunnel
According to forecasting analysis, the traffic accident probability within tunnel is
far less than that on ordinary road section (see Table 4-6-3). still such probability exists.
The hazardous cargo traffic accidents in tunnels are mainly the fire caused by the
explosion and burning of hazardous cargoes and pollution of tunnel air by hazardous and
poisonous gas, resulting in reduced the visibility. death, injury, traffic jam, traffic halt and
equipment breakdown. Besides, the tunnel structure can also cause some destruction.
4.8.4.5 Risk prevention of tunnel pollution
(1) The tunnel management station is responsible for the daily maintenance and repair
of the Yanggongshan and Fuziling tunnels and responsible for their normal operation and
control of their ventilation, lighting, fire warning, fire fighting. circuit TV. emergency
telephone and signal lamp. Also it is responsible for emergency handling in the tunnels.
(2) Tunnel management personnel should be trained. which will be incorporated into
the training prooram. so as to increase their ability to handle accident and to manage.
(3) Air within the tunnels should be monitored. which will be incorporated into the
environmental monitoring plan. and monitored data shall be reported timely.
(4) Management over hazardous substance transportation should be enhanced.
i, implementation of declaration system
;  implementation of sampling system
3  under bad weather. vehicles transporting hazardous substance are forbidden to
enter the tunnel.
The above K  and (  will be enforced by the tunnel management personnel.
4.8.4.6 Emergency plan for hazardous substance transportation accident
(I ) In case of emergency, any finder shall immediately notify the central monitor
*oom by the tunnel side telephone or other means.
(2) Upon receiving the accident, the central monitor room should immediately notify
he nearby highway patrol who will control the site. Meanwhile. nearby local fire fighting
iepartment should be also notified to help.
(3) If the hazardous substance is of solid form. thev can be cleaned and recorded in
he file.
(4) If the hazardous substance is of gas form and is fatally poisonous. firefighters
;hould wear masks to put out the fire. If the hazardous substance will unavoidably leak.
hen environmental and public security departments should be immediately notified to, if
lecessary. mobilize people within the pollution scope so as to prevent poisonous death.
100



(5) If the hazardous substance is of liquid form and has entered into public water
-odv. then environmental protection department should be immediately notified who will
ell the downstream units (especially the water supply plant) to stop take water, and
meanwhile will send environmental experts and monitors to the site to conduct
monitoring analysis, and to get the vessel from the water.
(6) Treatment measures for hazardous cargo accident in tunnel
In addition to the above treatment measures, for the treatment of hazardous cargo
accidents in tunnel. special emphasis shall be given to the clearing of site and inspection
and repairing of ventilation and alarming devices so as to eliminate the poisonous and
hazardous gases' pollution on environment.
4.8.4.7 Emergencv capability analysis for accident treatment
(1) In order to ensure driving safety under normal and emergency conditions. to
respond quickly to and to handle fire accident or other emergencies. to eliminate or
reduce pollution and damage caused by accidents. the tunnels are not only equipped with
necessary ventilation and lighting devices. but also with TV monitors. fire alarming and
.extinguishing facilities. It is intended to install 48 jet fans, 164 fire hydrants. 2 water feed
2quipment. The supervision and control system of tunnel is comprised of computer
.etwork. closed circuit TV monitor and comprehensive control panel.
2) The tunnel supervision and control program includes three conditions: normal. fire
nd accident. by which ventilation control, lighting and traffic control programs are set up.
Refer to the PreliminarY Design Chapter 8-Traffic Engineering cind Facility (MOC
R.esearch Institute of Highway. July 2000)
(3) The operation of the expressway (including tunnels) is under constant supervision.
\W hen accident happens. it can be known immediately and rescuing. firefighting.
nvironmental protection. traffic police can be notified quickly to handle it. Firefighting
mnd rescuing will be settled locally. Highway management authority shall keep contact
svith firefighting and medical department along the line and shall provide
elecommunication means.
(4) In order to better . strengthen the abilitv to cope with hazardous cargo
ransportation accidents. it is proposed that the World Bank Loan Project Office of JPCD
:onvene meetings. exchange experience. conduct training and study so as to improve
tbilits in coping with similar accidents. Damaged equipment shall be timely repaired.
naintained. installed and calibrate so as to put into use again.
To conclude. it can be thought that the project has a strong emergency handling
ibilitv of traffic accidents.

Chapter 5. Alternatives Analysis
5.1 "Without the Proposed Expressway" Alternative Analysis
National highway 105 is an important trunk road in Jiangxi province. With the
rapid economic development, there is an increasing of trading market, business
network. vehicle maintenance stations, petrol-oil station, even schools along the sides
of the highway 105. In 1997, about 92.37km out of the 257km in Ji' an prefecture
has become business street (accounting for 36%). Data in 1998 shows that the traffic
volume between Zhangshu-Nankang amounts to 4600-7500vehicle/day, mixed traffic
volume amounts to 4800-800vehicle/day, traffic congestion is 0.95-1.6. Due to the
increasing saturation, the average driving speed can only reach 40km/h with heavy
traffic jam and accidents. The increasing traffic also leads to the deterioration of the
surrounding acoustic and ambient air quality. In this regard, the building of the
proposed expressway will not only alleviate the traffic pressure. but at the same time
also improve the environmental quality along the national highway 105 .
5.2 Main Alignment Selection Procedure
The alignment is selected after comparison and optimization in three stages as
preliminary feasibility studv (Pre.F/S). feasibility study (F/S). and preliminary design
(as shown in figure 5-2-1).
5.3 Alternatives Comparison in Preliminary Feasibility Study
5.3.1 Impossibilitv of upgrading national highway 105
An analysis was done to the possibility in the preliminary feasibility study for
upgrading national highwav 105 to high-class highway. This alternative has the
following disadvantages:
(1) The mileage shall be increased a lot in order to avoid township. mines and
industrial areas. the alignment look no good;
(2) To avoid flood . the subgrade elevation shall be heightened as a whole, which
will cause serious environmental problem and waste of the existing resources.
(3) The widening of the subgrade will relocate a lot of buildings, power & tele.
lines. which will cause much negative impact on the industrial and agricultural
production as well as the living of the people along the route:
(4) The construction will further interrupt the traffic on highway 105 which in turn
increase traffic jam and accidents, causing social problems:
(5) Suichuan-Sadi of Ganzhou county is narrow hilly valley striking along the
river. big up and down in landform which gives no way for widening. If to do so,
there would be large excavation of the mountain slope or filling of the river bed which
will cause heavv soil erosion and water pollution , or even the danger of slope sliding
and flood jam:

(6) As most sections are plain area where there are high productive farmland,
widening the existing highway will occupy many good farnland which increase the
difficulty of land acquisition and compensation cost, causing big agricultural loss .
(7) Since there is no way to solve the mixed traffic interruption in nature, the
driving speed is still the same. Therefore. the purpose of upgrading the highway 105
to improve the vehicle operation efficiency is not preferable;
(8) Even if completed for operation, the environmental investment will be very
large since there are many sensitive locations as large residential quarters, townships,
schools, hospitals, etc. which need to build many sound barriers. In addition, these
103



sensitive locations will suffer more tail gas than present:
In sum, the upgrading alternative of highway 105 is not preferable from the point
of engineering, environmental protection and social respect.
5.3.2 Refuse to the East Ganjiang alignment alternative
This alternative starts from Taihe county, bypassing Wan' an, Xinguo, Ganxian,
Ganzhou city and ends at Nakang city. Complicated hilly landform gives difficulty to
project works; low class standard, long mileage for the main route; many structures,
two times overpass Ganjiang rive, two extreme large bridges shall be built; the
alignment doesn' t strike properly with Gan-Yue expressway as a whole. The
favorable terrain has been occupied by the  "Jing-Jiu"  railway and it, s very
difficult to line the expressway in addition to the interruption between each other.
Therefore, this alternative is not preferable in respect of engineering.
Looking from the point of social and environmental respect. this alternative has
the following shortcomings:
(I) The alignment goes in hilly area, bypassing a long mileage of heavy soil
erosion areas where the construction will further worsen the situation. As large
quantities of earth & stone works, earth borrowing and waste area are required. there
would be a lot of investment in protection and greening works.
(2) Tow-time overpassing the Ganjiang river, the construction will on the exert
impact on the water quality. What, s more, the transport of hazardous subjects in
operation phase will have high potential risk in polluting the river water. There are
many big or small townships on the banks, the water pollution will cause social
unrest.
(3) The favorable terrain is very narrow with few farmlands. As the "Jing-Jiu
railway construction has already occupied many of the farmland, another
expressway will reduce the farmland even more, resulting in big agricultural loss. In
this regard, it is difficult to get the public support.
(4) The overlapping of the two trunk lines is unfavorable to the play of transport
efficiency, which result in small social benefits.
5.3.3 Comparison of West Ganjiang Alignment Alternative
5.3.3.1 Brief of the alternative
After refuse to the above two alternatives. the preliminary F/S report put forward
the following three alternatives (Refer to Figure 5-3-1):
(I) Alternative I (Recommended Scheme)
The proposed expressway starts from the end point of the Changfu-Taihe section -
- Nlashi township (the intersection point with the national highway 105). and ends at
the Longling Town of Nankang city intersected with highway 105 (or 323). The

5.5 Partial alignment optimization in construction design phase
Partial alignment optimization has been done in construction design phase with a
total distance of 40km, equivalent to 30 percent of the total mileage of the main line.
According to the survey. there are no major environmental factors such as wetland,
wild animal living area, natural protection zone, etc. among the 9 optimized sections.
The details concerning the work quantities, rationality of adjustments and
environmental factors for the 9 optimized sections are presented in Table 5-5-1-Table
5-5-3 .

Chapter 6. Environmental Management Plan
6.1 Environmental management plan
6.1.1 Implementation organizations
The environmental management for the proposed expressway is organized by the
Jiangxi Province Communication Department (JPCD) and implemented by the World
Bank Loan Project Office of JPCD. The organizations of the environmental
management in the construction and the operation period are shown in Figure 6-1-1
and Figure 6-1-2 respectively.
Planning Division of JPCD (3 persons)

119



The Environmental Protection Office of the MOC is responsible for coordination
of the environmental protection work in communication sector.
The Planning Division of Jiangxi Provincial Communications Department (JPCD)
is responsible for the environmental protection work in this sector in the province,
including formulation of environmental protection measures and rules, the provincial
environmental protection plan and supervision of the implementation of the
environmental protection plan.
The World Bank Loan Project Office under JPCD is the executive organization of
this project. On May 5, 2000, it sets up a leadership team coordinating engineering,
environmental and resettlement affaires. under it there are environmental protection
team and resettlement team staffed with 3-6 personnel with one environmental expert.
The responsibilities are as follows.
(1) To prepare the EIA report and EAP;
(2) Be in charge of environmental management and resettlement arrangement for
the proposed project;
(3) To implement the environmental protection in accordance with the terms
under the contract, in cooperation with the environmental protection engineer. to
provide information concerning the environmental protection measures implemented
in the construction period;
(4) To enter into environmental monitoring contract with the local environmental
monitoring station and supervise the monitoring work, to supervise the
implementation of the environmental monitoring plan and report the implementations
and the monitoring report;
(5) To coordinate the relations between the environmental protection engineer.
the contractor. and the design unit;
(6) To deal with the complains concerning the environmental protection and to
accept the supervision of the environmental protection department;
(7) To purchase mobile automatic noise level detector to monitor the noise level
in the construction period and the operation period and report the monitoring work:
In the construction period. each of the contract section will be staffed with one
environmental supervision engineer. totaling 9 engineers for 9 contract sections),
whose responsibilities are:
(I) To supervise the implementation of the environmental protection measures as
specified under the EAP and the bidding document;
(2) To monitor the noise level during the construction period
During the construction period. the contractor shall appoint more than one person
120



responsible for environmental protection work, with the responsibilities as follows.
(1) To implement the environmental protection works and measures during the
construction phase as specified in the contract and the bidding document;
(2) To cooperate with the environmental protection supervision engineer to
inspect and check the environmental protection work for the construction work.
A number of 3 highway management office are to be established when the
proposed expressway is completed. In each of the highway management offices there
will be one person to be responsible for the environmental protection work for the
concerned section.
6.1.2 Environmental management plan
To guarantee the implementation of the environmental protection measures, an
environmental management plan has been set up as shown in Table 6-1-1.

6.1.2 Supervision organization
The Jiangxi Provincial Environmental Protection Bureau (JPEPB) is the
competent authority under the Provincial People' s Government responsible for
supervision and management of the environmental protection in Jiangxi province.
There are local EPBs at regional, municipal, county levels responsible for the
environmental protection in their administrative jurisdiction areas. In the PEPB there
is Environmental Protection Monitoring Center; and under the regional and municipal
EPB, there is Environmental Monitoring Station (EMS). The environmental
protection work for the proposed expressway will be carried out under the supervision
of the local EPB along the highway areas. The detailed environmental protection
mana-gement plan refers to the environmental supervision plan, as shown in Table 6-
.-.

6.2 Environmental Monitoring Plan
(1) Purpose and principles
The purpose of environmental monitoring plan is to implement each of the
environmental protection measures and to adjust envirornmental plan in time
according to the monitored result, to provide evidence and basis for arrangement of
the time schedule of the protection measures. The principle of the environmental
monitoring plan is based on the expected main environmental impact in different
periods (construction or operation period).
(2) Monitoring items
The environmental impacts are mainly in the construction and operation periods.
In the construction period, the impacts mainly are TSP, bitumen smoke, construction
noise and water quality. In the operation period, the impacts mainly are traffic noise,
ambient air and water environment.
According to the forecast and the assessment, the items to be monitored are TSP.
bitumen smoke, construction noise and water quality in the construction period: and in
the operation period, the traffic noise. ambient air and the water quality.
(3) Environmental monitoring organization
In construction period, the supersvision engineer shall undertake the noise
monitoring. The other environmental monitoring work shall be contracted out to the
Ji' an and Ganzhou EMSs. To ensure implementation of the monitoring plan. the
Project owner shall enter into contract before commencement of the construction w ith
the EMS concerning the monitoring in the construction period; and shall enter into
another contract before the hand over of the completed highway with the EMS
concerning the monitoring work in the operation period.
(4) Enxvironmental monitoring plan
The environmental monitoring plan is summarized in Table 6-1-2.
(5) Cost estimation of the environmental monitoring equipment and fee
Five noise monitoring instrument shall be purchased for this project. which costs
about RMB 100.000.
The environmental monitoring fee in the construction period are about
RMB270.000: the environmental monitoring fee in the operation period is about
RMB210.000 (refer to Table 6-2-1 for details).The total monitoring costs about
RMB480.000.
129



Table 6-2-1 Monitoring Cost
NPhase    Construction Phase     Operation Phase         Remarks

The economic assessment for the proposed expressway project includes national
economic evaluation, financial analysis and sensitivity analysis. The assessment
results of each indicator are listed in Table 7-1-1 -Table 7-1-3.
It can be seen from  Table 7-1-1  -Table7-1-3 that this project has a relatively
good economic benefit and financial return as well as strong risk resistance ability.

Chapter 8    Public Participation
8.1 Outline of Public Participation and Negotiation
As an important project in Jiangxi province, the proposed Taihe-Ganzhou
highway, after being completed, will play an vital importance in connecting the
Yangtze economic zone and south China economic special zones, in supplementing
the national highway networks, in satisfying traffic increase. It is particularly
important to meet Jiangxi province' s economic growth and to perfect economic
pattern, to expedite the exploration and utilization of the province' s tourism
resources and to promote the whole province, s social and economic development.
The preliminary preparations for this highway have already attracted wide attention
from every circles of the society.
The Jiangxi provincial government strongly supports the project. the Ji' an
prefecture and the Ganzhou city government and their transportation departments
have actively participated in the preliminary preparation works. City and county
governments along the line also expressed their concern and support to the project and
have suggested many helpful ideas to the alignment.
In order to fully comprehend the public opinions and to really protect the interests
of influenced people. the concerned departments of construction. design. resettlement
and environmental assessment unit have made four public participation surveys and
consultation on Dec. 10-15. 1999. April 12-20, 2000. and Mav 18-June 5, 2000 and
Nov. 20-28.2000 respectively. The latest (fourth) public survey was carried out for
those impacted by the optimized alignment in the construction design for the
recommended scheme. The survey places are cities. counties and townships along the
proposed line. In the process of data collection and site visiting, the assessment team.
resettlement office and the design department consulted with relevant departments as
agriculture. statistics. water conservation. forestry. environmental protection and
communications. etc. Through public investigation and consultation, we have
obtained information about the current social and economic conditions along the road.
listened to the opinions and suggestions of the experts and the public concerned. The
team has also informed them the proposed project and its environmental protection
progress. thus increasing the popularity of the project and gaining strong support and
coordination  from   governmental  organizations.  social  organizations.  non-
governmental organizations and the public.
8.1.1 Survey method and respondent
The public participation survey was carried out in three different forms.
(1) Family or individual interview
134



The respondents are those families who may be directly affected by the project
(to be resettled. or involved in land acquisition) and the resident representatives who
are impacted by the hauling vehicles' noise close to the excess road and the national
highway 105 . The major villages being surveyed are: Nitang, Huangzhangduan,
Zhuhu, Kangfu. Yuziqian, Wuche, Mawei, Baijia, Zhangtang,Shaoxi.Xitou, Sheqian.
Gaoshan. Xiawan,Zhongshe, etc. (see Table 8-1 -1).
The surveyer first of all gave them a brief introduction about the alignment of the
proposed expressway and the possible positive effects (improvement in transportation
infrastructure, economic development) and negative effects (possible land acquisition,
removal, resettlement and traffic noise) brought out by the highway. Then the
respondents filled a public opinion form (household) at their will, or orally expressed
their opinion which have been recorded by the questionnaires, then summarized and
analyzed by the investigators.
(2) Group interview
The respondents are mainly village committees and schools that may be affected
along the road. Seminars or filling of form were held in which individual gave free
talks. then summarized into the public opinion representing the unit. The interviwed
units are mainly Sanjiang town, Daping township. Jingshi township. Luogang
township. Wuling High School, Mashuang High School, Nankang dermatopathy
Clinic. Sheshang sholl, Hongshan school, Zhangtang school Shaoxi school. etc.. refer
to Table 8-1 -1 for details
(3) Seminar with governmental and non-governmental organizations
The owner. design. resettlement and environmental assessment units have visited
local agriculture, statistics. hydro, forestry. environmental protection  and
communications departments, gathered opinions and data from each department,
also convened a meeting in Taihe on August 25. 2000 attended by governmental or
non-governmental organizations as influenced people. women representative. teachers,
political  consulters,  people' s  representatives.  transportation  bureau  and
environmental protection bureau. Due to the partial alignment optimization in the
recommended scheme. another meeting was held on November 30. 2000 in Jii an
which was attended by governmental or non-governmental organizations as
influenced people, women representative. teachers. political consulters. people' s
representatives. transportation bureau, environmental protection bureau and the
resident representatives who are impacted by the hauling vehicles' noise close to the
excess road and the national highway 105. The memorandum of the two meetings is
shown in Annex III.
The topics of the meeting include:
135



,  Introduction of the necessity, construction scale and technical standard of the
proposed expressway by the owner;
20 Basic principle in selecting the alignment and coordination with local opinion;
Æ3 Major environmental concerns of the project and possible removal and
resettlement problems.
The attendants have put forward many precious opinions for this project, which
have been reflected in the design documents, EIA report or RAP.
During the previous three public surveys, a total of 420 family questionnaires
were distributed and 367 were returned back, accounting for 87.4% of the total; 32
group questionnaires were distributed with 30 returned back, accounting for 93.8% of
the total. The survey involved 491 persons (based on the family). 55 villages, 12
organizations. (note: some of the places or respondents may be overlapped in the first
three surveys, see Table 8-1-1) . The fourth (latest) public survey distributes 98 family
questionnaires were distributed and 83 were returned back, accounting for 84.7% of
the total; 15 group questionnaires were distributed with 13 returned back. accounting
for 86.7% of the total. The survey involved 83 person (based on the family). 14
villages, refer to Table 8-1-2 for details.
The memorandum for influenced people, governmental and non-governmental
organizations are shown in Annex III.

8.1.2 Survey content and the result statistics
(I) To give an brief introduction of the proposed highway, including its necessity.
alignmrent, construction scale and technical standard, as well as the principle in
selecting alternative schemes, etc..
(2) To outlines the main environmental concerns of the proposed expressway by
the environmental assessment department to the public and to introduce the protection
measures to be adopted.
(3) To give an introduction of the national and local policies conceming land
acquisition, resettlement, and compensations.
(4) To solicit public, s recommendations and requests regarding the expressway
construction, its environmental impacts and mitigation measures.
